# Fel Dwarf Compendium

The Fel Dwarves are a cruel and pitiless race, their hearts blackened by centuries of tyranny, conquest, and infernal corruption. Once noble kin to other dwarves, they long ago severed all ties to honor, embracing fiendish sorcery and ruthless industry. Now, they stand as brutal overlords, ruling through fear, slavery, and an insatiable hunger for power. To them, strength is law, cruelty is virtue, and conquest is purpose.

This corruption has reshaped not just their minds but their bodies as well. Their blackened, gnarled features are marked with deep cracks, as if scorched by fire. Many sport horn-like protrusions, jagged spines, or ridged skulls, grim testaments to their dark pacts. Some have smoldering beards, wreathed in embers or slick with alchemical oils, while their glowing eyes burn with a cold, calculating malice.

**Masters of the Infernal Depths.** Fel Dwarves carve their empires from the most inhospitable and hellish landscapes, thriving in volcanic wastelands, abyssal caverns, and cursed ruins. Their obsidian citadels, choked with smoke, rise from these hellish domains, their forges burning without end. Beneath them, endless hordes of slaves toil in misery, crafting weapons, war machines, and daemon-forged horrors under the lash.

Their society is a brutal hierarchy, ruled by Demon-Smith Prophets, sorcerer-engineers who command with unquestioned authority.

Beneath them, warlords, priests, and slavedrivers enforce their will, ensuring that the empire’s gears of conquest never cease turning. The weak are fuel for the empire, whether as laborers, sacrifices, or experiments in their ever-growing arsenal of war.

**Conquerors and Slavers.** Fel Dwarves do not simply invade and conquer—they strip the land bare. Entire civilizations are crushed, their people shackled and their cities ground into dust. Those who resist are slaughtered; those who surrender face eternal servitude in the factories, mines, and forges of the empire.

On the battlefield, they combine relentless discipline with unholy war machines, unleashing heavily armored warriors, fiendish artillery, and demonic constructs in devastating waves of destruction. Their black iron legions march with mechanical precision, their siege engines belching fire and molten metal as their sorcerer-priests call upon dark gods for destruction.

**A Legacy of Ruin.** Though their empire is vast and unmatched, Fel Dwarves are not without enemies. Slave revolts, rival demon cults, and their own insatiable hunger for power threaten to consume them from within. The very forces they wield grow unstable, their bound daemons straining against their chains.

Yet they do not fear collapse. They welcome destruction, believing that in the end, only the strongest will reshape the world in their image. Until that day comes, they will continue their conquest, leaving only ashes and ruin in their wake.

## Running Fel Dwarf Encounters
The setting you’re running your adventures in will help determine the background of this dwarven race and the specifics of their lore. In some settings, they may be twisted by the forces of fel into malevolent beings. If your setting has a cosmology aligned with more classical D&D settings, these dwarves will likely align themselves with devils, given that they share a lawful evil and tyrannical nature. 

### Fel Dwarf Motivations and Adventure Setups

Regardless of the lore and setting specifics, these dwarves are defined by their conquering industrialist nature. Players could encounter and come into conflict with fel dwarves under many types of circumstances. You can use the table on the next page as inspiration for ways to introduce fel dwarves into your campaign:


##### Fel Dwarf Adventure Setups

| d8  | Setup |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Resource Contention:** Fel dwarves are relentless in their pursuit of valuable resources, such as precious metals, gems, or magical artifacts. Players might find themselves competing with these malevolent beings for control of a recently discovered mine, an ancient ruin, or a forgotten vault. |
|  2  | **Servitude and Oppression:** Fel dwarves are notorious for their brutal treatment of captured laborers and conquered peoples. Players might be tasked with liberating enslaved individuals or communities, or they may find themselves captured by the fel dwarves and forced to fight for their freedom. |
|  3  | **Tyrannical Conquerers:** Players may be visiting frontier towns in danger of being conquered and enslaved by an invasion force of fel dwarves on the march.  |
|  4  | **Dark Alliances:** Fel dwarves are known to forge alliances with other malevolent forces, such as fiendish entities, evil warlords, or twisted cults. Players may cross paths with fel dwarves while investigating or combating these dark forces. |
|  5  | **Magical Catastrophes:** Fel dwarves wield a potent combination of arcane power and technological prowess. Their experiments and machinations can sometimes result in magical disasters, which could threaten the players' homeland or disrupt the balance of power in the region. |
|  6  | **Exploration and Adventure:** Players venturing into the dark and inhospitable regions where fel dwarves dwell may stumble upon their citadels or outposts.  |


\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

|   |  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  7  | **Intrigue and Subterfuge:** Fel dwarves are cunning and manipulative, and they may infiltrate other societies to further their nefarious goals. Players might be tasked with unmasking a fel dwarf spy or uncovering a plot to destabilize a city or kingdom.
|  8  | **Ancient Grudges:** Many fel dwarves bear long-standing grudges against their noble kin, and they may actively seek to undermine or destroy dwarven settlements or interests. Players aligned with dwarven factions may be called upon to defend against fel dwarf incursions or sabotage. |

### Roleplaying Fel Dwarves

Fel dwarves are ambitious power seekers, always looking to advance themselves above others. They view other races with contempt, seeing their kind as superior to all others. Fel dwarves meeting the players will either see them as a means to an end or as obstacles to be destroyed. They may be willing to trade with the players, but if the players are aligned with forces opposed to the interest of the fel dwarves or their masters, they will likely turn on the players before long.  

Consider these traits when playing on the decisions and behavior of fel dwarves. They are not reckless barbarians, but calculating tyrants, always looking for that chance to further their machinations, enhance their wealth, or advance in power. That said, they still value loyalty to their masters, and though they scheme and plot their way up through their hierarchies, fel dwarves will carry out their assigned duties without question. For it is through this loyalty and cold, calculating devotion they hope to advance in power.

### Fel Dwarf Tactics
In combat, fel dwarves are stubborn, brutal, and capable of executing complex tactics utilizing a mix of different units. The fel dwarf forces can include many types of soldiers, machines, and creatures, but there are tactical trends that can be found through most of their kind:

***Low Mobility.*** Like most dwarven forces, fel dwarves fight best when they can force their enemies to come to them. They often make use of monsters and more mobile soldiers of other races to compensate for their lack of speed. Still, even these forces perform best when attacking foes already tangled up in combat with the elite fel dwarf soldiers.

***Heavy Firepower.*** Like many of their dwarven kin, fel dwarves are master crafters and engineers. They create advanced firearms and artillery weapons imbued with fiendish power, which they bring to bare on their foes whenever possible.

***Mixed Forces.*** Between their heavy infantry, masses of expendable laborers, mobile creatures, menacing monsters, diabolic magic, and technically advanced firearms and war machines, fel dwarves have a multitude of options at their disposal. And they excel at combining these forces in ways that offset their weaknesses.

***Enslavers.*** Fel dwarf society runs on the back of forced labor, and they are always in need of more workers. Fel dwarves avoid killing enemies in combat when it can feasibly be avoided. Defeated foes are transported back to the nearest fel dwarf settlement, where they are quickly put to work.

***Heartless Discipline.*** Fel dwarves possess the same level of resolve as their uncorrupted kin and will carry out battle plans to a tee, even putting themselves in danger to do so. To do anything less is considered a sign of weakness, and there is nothing fel dwarves despise more than weakness.

\columnbreak

#### Engagement
Dwarves prefer to force their enemies to engage them. They will attempt to bombard foes with superior firepower to force an approach. Ideally, this allows the heavy dwarven infantry to engage their foes without needing to move to make the engagement themselves. This means of combat initiation is rarely subtle, and fel dwarves typically do not attempt to sneak up on their enemies unless they’re utilizing stealthier minions of other races.

#### Combat
In battle, fel dwarves seek to outlast their foes with durable creatures or masses of laborers while brutally breaking them into submission through superior firepower. They seek to establish a superior position in battle from which they can withstand any attacks while laying waste to their foes. What position they take and how they bring down their foes will depend on the creatures and weapons the fel dwarves have at their disposal. They rarely fight with only one type of creature and usually rely on mixing strategies to offset exploitable weaknesses.

#### Retreat
Fel dwarves are stubborn, but they aren’t stupid. If they see that their strategy has been countered, they may retreat to regroup and gather what they need to overcome their foes. If fel dwarves suffer heavy losses, they will retreat to a more defensible position while calling for backup. 
If their enemies are retreating, the fel dwarves will pursue them whenever possible, as defeated and fleeing foes present a prime opportunity for rounding up new laborers.

## New Fel Dwarf Weapons
Fel dwarves are known for their wicked ingenuity and have invented destructive firearms beyond the capabilities of most other races. The following firearm weapons are used by some of the fel dwarf infantry described later and can be made available to players at the DM’s discretion. 

***Blunderbuss.*** Crafted in the dark forges of the fel dwarves, blunderbusses are marvels of dark engineering, combining the dwarven knack for craftsmanship with cruel, destructive intent. Larger and more potent than the firearms wielded by their kin, these weapons are loaded with a lethal mix of shot, black powder, and arcane substances. When fired, they unleash devastating projectiles capable of decimating enemy ranks and piercing the strongest armor.

***Fire Glaive.*** These infernal weapons combine the melee capabilities of a traditional glaive with a rifle capable of shooting flaming projectiles. Fire glaives are rare and expensive to produce and, as such, are only used by the most elite fel dwarf soldiers. Soldiers utilizing these weapons are able to act as hybrid warriors, alternating between melee and ranged combat depending on the needs of the battle.

#### Blunderbuss
*ranged weapon (martial)*
___
- **Damage:** 3d10
- **Damage Type:** Piercing
- **Properties:** Ammunition (range 80/320), reload (1), heavy, two-handed
- **Cost:** 75 gp
- **Weight:** 18 lb.

\columnbreak

<br><br>



#### Fire Glaive
*melee weapon (martial)*
___
- **Damage:** 1d10
- **Damage Type:** Piercing
- **Properties:** ammunition (range 100/400), heavy, reach, reload (1), two-handed, special
- **Cost:** 125 gp
- **Weight:** 18 lb
___

### New Weapon Properties 
&emsp;**Fire Glaive.** This weapon can be used to make ranged attacks that use its ammunition property. Attacks made this way deal an additional 1d10 fire damage on hit.

**Reload (X).**  This weapon can be fired X times before it must be reloaded using an action or in place of an attack that's part of an attack action or in place of an off-hand attack while duel wielding. The weapon can be reloaded early without losing any ammunition.

<br>

# New Spells

## Lore of Death

This brand of magic plays on the nature of mortality and fragility of life, though it is strictly distinct from traditional necromancy, as it embraces the inevitability of death rather than attempting to deny it. Its users can manipulate negative energy, sap the vitality of foes, and instill mortal terror in those around them. The following spells are examples of the types of magic users of the Lore of Death often wield.

#### Aspect of Dread
*2nd-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A white feather)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard, Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard 
___

A wave of terrifying specters spill out form a creature you can within range in a 10-foot emanation. Every other creature within the emanation must make a Wisdom saving throw or become frightened of the target for the duration.
A creature frightened in this way can make a Wisdom saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself with a success.

***Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot*** The emanation increases by 10 feet for each slot level above 3.


#### Crippling Pain
*3rd-level necromancy*

- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A broken bone)
- **Duration:**  1 round
- **Classes:**  Cleric Warlock, Wizard

You afflict a creature within you can see range within range to be wracked with pain. The target must make a Constitution saving throw.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br>

On a failed save, every time the creature takes a move, an action, a bonus action, or a reaction, before the start of your next turn, it takes 4d8 necrotic damage.
 
 On a successful save, it takes 2d8 necrotic damage instead.

**Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot.** You can target one additional creature for each spell slot level above 3


#### Horrifying Laughter
*6th-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 30 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A tiny tarts and a feather that is waved in the air)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard, Wizard
___

You cause a creature you can see within range to suffer debilitating fits of deranged laughter. The target must make a wisdom saving throw. On a failed save, the target takes 3d10 force damage, fall prone, and become incapacitated and unable to stand for the duration. On a successful save, the target takes half as much damage, and the spell ends.

A creatures that starts it's turn within 30 feet of the laughing creature and can hear the laughter must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or become frightened of the laughing creature until the start of its next turn. You can choose any number of creatures you can see to be immune to this effect.

For the duration, the target makes a Wisdom saving throw at the start of each of your turns. On a failed save, it takes the force damage again. On a successful save, the spell ends. If damage from this spell reduces the target to 0 hit points, it stabilizes but remains laughing and can no longer attempt saving throws against the spell. If the spell ends while the creature has 0 hit points, it dies.

***Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot*** The the force damage increase by 1d10 for each spell slot level above 6.

 <img src='https://m.media-amazon.com/images/I/51+A6aJV1lL.jpg' style='position:absolute;right:-16px;top:-110px;width:848px;transform:scaleX(-1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
style='position:absolute;right:-280px;top:-15px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(192deg)' />

#### Impending Doom 
*4th-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A black feather)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard, Cleric, Warlock 
___

You target a creature within range, sapping its determination and resolve to go on. The target must make a Charisma saving throw. On a failed save, the creature is filled with a sense of impending doom, and for the duration, whenever it makes an attack roll, ability check, or saving throw against an effect not triggered by this spell, it can't gain advantage on the roll and it automatically misses or fails if the roll is 6 or lower, as the creature feels an overwhelming sense of defeat.

The affected creature can make a Charisma saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the spell's effect on a success.

**Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot.** You can target one additional creature for each spell slot level above 4.

####  Purple Sun
*9th-level transmutation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 120 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A pinch of lime, water, and earth)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard
___

You conjure a grim sphere of purple light at a point you designate within range. The sphere has a maximum radius of 60 feet and illuminates its area with dim light.

Any creature that either enters the sphere's area for the first time on its turn or begins its turn inside the sphere must make a Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, the creature is petrified for the duration. At the end of <br> each of its turns, the target can make another <br> Constitution saving throw. On a success, the <br> spell ends on the target. However, if a creature <br> accumulates three failed saves against this <br> spell (including the initial failed save), it <br> remains petrified indefinitely until the <br> condition is cured by other means.

If a petrified creature is physically <br> damaged or broken during this state, it <br> will manifest the same damage upon <br> being reverted to its original form.

<br>

#### Lore of Death Art Credit
* Cavalier of Night - Viktor Titov, <br> Wizards of the Coast
* Damnation - Kev Walker, <Br> Wizards of the Coast

\columnbreak

#### Spirit Leech
*1st-level necromancy*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A mosquito)
- **Duration:**  1 hour
- **Classes:**  Warlock
___

You reach out and drain the life force of a target creature you can see within range. The target must make a Charisma saving throw. On a failed save, it takes 1d12 necrotic damage, or half as much on a successful one. You gain temporary hit points equal to the damage dealt. Constructs are immune to this spell's effects.

***Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot*** The the necrotic damage increase by 1d12 for each spell slot level above 1.

#### Wind of Death
*5th-level necromancy*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** Self
- **Components:** V, S, M (A owl feather)
- **Duration:**  Instantaneous
- **Classes:**  Cleric
___

You release unholy wind in a 60-foot-long, 15-foot-wide line in a direction of your choice. Each creature within the line must make a Constitution saving throw. A creature takes 5d6 cold damage and 5d6 necrotic damage on a failed save, and half as much on a success.

***Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot.*** The cold damage and the necrotic damage increase by 1d6 for each spell slot level above 5.

## Lore of Fire

This brand of magic draws on the power of elemental fire. This arcane fire is often fueled by powerful emotions, and those who wield it are often known for their reckless and headstrong behavior. By channeling their fiery nature into their magic, these pyromancers can unleash an array of devastating spells capable of burning foes to cinders. These spells all tend to conjure and manipulate fire in some way and are very aggressive in nature. The following spells are examples of the types of magic users of the Lore of Fire often wield.

#### Burning Bolts
*6th-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 100 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (A burnt stick)
- **Duration:** Instant
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Wizard

Choose up to three directions. A line of flames 100 feet long and 5 feet wide emanates from you in each direction you choose. Each creature in a line must make a Dexterity saving throw. A creature takes 7d10 fire damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. A creature in the area of more than one line is affected only once.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 7th level or higher, you can create one additional line of flames for each slot level above 6th.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

#### Burning Head
*5th-level conjuration*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (A bit of tallow, a pinch of brimstone, and a dusting of powdered iron)
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard

A 5-foot-diameter flaming head appears in an unoccupied space of your choice within range and lasts for the duration. When the head appears, it lets out a terrifying screech. Creatures of your choice that can see and hear the head within 100 feet of it must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or become frightened of the head until the spell ends. If a frightened creature ends its turn in a location where it doesn’t have line of sight to the head, it can repeat the saving throw, ending the effect on itself on a success.

**Contact With The Head.** Any creature that ends its turn within 5 feet of the head must make a Dexterity saving throw. The creature takes 3d8 fire damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. 

**Moving The Head.** As a bonus action, you can move the head up to 30 feet. If you ram the head into a creature, that creature must make the saving throw against the head’s damage, and the head stops moving this turn. When you move the head, you can direct it over barriers up to 5 feet tall and jump it across pits up to 10 feet wide. The head ignites flammable objects not being worn or carried, and it sheds bright light in a 20-foot radius and dim light for an additional 20 feet.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 6th level or higher, the damage increases by 1d8 for each slot level above 5th.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/H2bZkRH/Incendiary-Flow-Eldritch-Moon-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-0px; right:-80px; width:1000px;' />
 
 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:-90px;top:100px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(180deg)' />


\pagebreakNum



#### Conflagration

*4th-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 ft
- **Components:** V
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Wizard

Choose one creature you have seen within the last minute. If the creature is within range, it is engulfed in an inferno. The target takes 4d6 fire damage and is set on fire for the spell’s duration. The burning target sheds bright light in a 30-foot radius and dim light for an additional 30 feet, and it can’t benefit from being invisible.

At the end of each of the creature's turns while on fire, it takes 4d6 fire damage.

**Extinguishing The Fire.** A creature can use its action to douse the fire by making a Dexterity check against your spell save DC. On a success, the flames are extinguished. The flames are also extinguished if the creature is fully submerged in water or standing in an area with strong wind (at least 20 miles per hour). 

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 5th level or higher, you can target one additional creature for each slot level above 4th. All the creatures must be within 30 feet of each other when you target them.


#### Flame Arrows
*3rd-level transmutation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 bonus action
- **Range:** Touch
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 hour
- **Classes:** Artificer, Druid, Ranger, Sorcerer, Wizard, 
___

You touch up to twelve arrows or bolts. When a target is hit by a ranged weapon attack using one of these pieces of ammunition, the target takes an extra 1d6 fire damage, and if it is a flammable object, it is ignited. The spell’s magic ends on the piece of ammunition when it hits or misses a target, and the spell ends when all the ammunition has lost its magic.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 4th level or higher, the number of pieces of ammunition you can affect with this spell increases by two for each slot level above 3rd.


#### Flame Blade
*2nd-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** Self
- **Components:** V, S M (leaf of sumac)
- **Duration:** Up to 10 minutes
- **Classes:** Druid, Sorcerer
___

You evoke a fiery blade, similar in size and shape to a scimitar, in your free hand. When you cast this spell, you may make two melee spell attacks with the blade against any targets within your reach. On a hit, a target takes fire damage equal to 1d6 + your spellcasting ability modifier. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

The blade remains for the spell's duration. If you let go of the blade, it disappears, but you can evoke the blade again as a bonus action. You can make the two attacks with the blade again on each of your turns as an action. The flaming blade sheds bright light in a 10-foot radius and dim light for an additional 10 feet.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 4th level or higher, you may make one additional attack with the blade per action for every two slot levels above 2nd.


#### Flame Cage
*6th-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 120 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (A small piece of phosphorus)
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Wizard

You choose a point on a solid surface within range, causing a cage made of opaque flames in the shape of a cube to appear. The cube can be up to 30 feet on each side, and it lasts for the duration. 

**Creatures Caught Partially Within the Cage.** When the cage is created, creatures only partially within the cube's area, or those too large to fit inside the area, must choose to be pushed away from the center of the area until they are completely outside the area or move into the cage if they can fit. 

**Creatures In The Cage When It Forms.** Any creature fully within the cage when it forms (including those that chose to move inside it) must make a Dexterity saving throw. A target takes 7d8 fire damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. 

**Moving Through The Cage.** A creature takes the 7d8 fire damage when it passes through a side of the cube for the first time on a turn.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 7th level or higher, the damage increases by 1d8 for each slot level above 6th.

##### Lore of Fire Art Credit
* Incendiary Flow - Raymond Swanland, Wizards of the Coast
* Annihilating Fire - Clint Cearley, Wizards of the Coast

## Lore of Fel Dwarves
This fiendish magic was developed by the devil-worshipping fel dwarves and embodies their ability to dominate not only the will of others but the very earth itself. Many of their spells conjure a brutal mix of fire and earth, incinerating or crushing foes with molten rock. Other spells twist the will of others, instilling deep hatred or fear and subservience. While these spells are most commonly used by fel dwarves, other fiendish spell casters or those with close ties to fire and earth may wield this magic as well.

#### Ash Storm

*5th-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60
- **Components:** V, S, M (a pinch of soot)
- **Duration:**  Instantaneous
- **Classes:**  Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard

You unleash a wave of scalding ash in a 60-foot-long, 15-foot-wide line originating from you in a direction you choose. Each creature in the line must make a Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 5d10 fire damage, is pushed 15 feet away form you, and is blinded until the end of your next turn. On a successful save, a creature takes half as much damage and suffers no other effect.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 5th level or higher, the fire damage increases by 1d10 and for each slot level above 4th.



\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

#### Breath of Hatred
*1st-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 ft
- **Components:** V
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard, Warlock

Your breath fills a creature with obsessive malice. Choose one creature within range. The target must make a Wisdom saving throw (it may choose to fail), or it becomes obsessed* with another creature of your choice within range that is hostile to the target. While obsessed, the target has advantage on attack rolls against the chosen creature.

At the end of each of its turns, the target can make another Wisdom saving throw. If it did not take an action during the turn or the source of its obsession is not within line of sight, it has advantage on the saving throw. On a success, the spell ends.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 3rd level or higher, you can target one additional creature to become obsessed with the same creature for every two slot levels above 1st.

#### Curse of Stone

*4th-level transmutation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60
- **Components:** V, S, M (a pinch of lime, water, and earth)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute.
- **Classes:**  Druid, Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard

You attempt to transform one creature that you can see within range into stone. If the target’s body is made of flesh, it must make a Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, the creature is petrified until the spell ends.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 5th level or higher, you can target one additional creature for ever two slots levels above 4th. The creatures must be within 30 feet of each other when you target them.

#### Divine Hammer
*6th-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 150 ft
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:** Instantaneous
- **Classes:**  Cleric

Choose a point you can see on the ground within range and a direction. A giant hammer manifests and slams the ground at the chosen point, impacting everything in a 10-foot cube centered on the point. It then sends a 30-foot-long, 10-foot-wide shockwave in the chosen direction before disappearing.

Each creature in the area of the hammer’s impact or shockwave must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 5d6 fire or lighting damage (your choice) and 5d6 thunder damage and is knocked prone; it is also dazed* until the end of its next turn if it is in the area of the impact. On a successful save, a creature takes half as much damage and isn’t knocked prone or dazed.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 7th level or higher, the fire or lighting damage and the thunder damage each increase by 1d6 for every slot level above 6th.


#### Elemental Bane (Revised)

*2nd-level transmutation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 bonus action
- **Range:** 90
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute.
- **Classes:**  Druid, Warlock, Wizard, Artificer

Choose one creature you can see within range and one of the following damage types: acid, cold, fire, lightning, or thunder. The target must succeed on a Charisma saving throw or be cursed for the duration. While cursed, the target loses any resistance to the chosen damage type, and immunity to the damage type is treated as resistance instead. Additionally, the first time each turn the target takes damage of the chosen type, it takes an extra 1d6 damage of that type.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 3rd level or higher, you can target one additional creature for each slot level above 2nd. The creatures must be within 30 feet of each other when you target them.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

> #####  Divine Hammer Damage Types
> Depending on the nature of the god the spellcaster worships, it may make more sense for the divine hammer to do damage of a type other than fire or lighting; for example, some gods may be more associated with radiant or necrotic. At the DM's discretion, the damage can be changed this way, in which case the spellcaster should no longer have the option for fire or lighting.

<br>

#### Eruption
*8th-level evocation*

- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 150 ft
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:** Instantaneous
- **Classes:**   Druid, Wizard, Sorcerer

You choose a point you can see on the ground within range. The ground cracks and a burst of magma erupts in a 60-foot-radius, 120-foot-high cylinder centered on that point. Each creature in the affected area must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 4d12 fire damage and 4d12 bludgeoning damage. On a successful save, it takes half as much damage.

Additionally, the ground in the area becomes superheated for 1 minute. The area becomes difficult terrain, and any creature that ends its turn in the area must make a Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, the creature takes 4d12 fire damage, or half as much on a successful save.

After the area cools down, it remains difficult terrain until cleared. Each 5-foot-square portion of the area requires at least 1 minute to clear by hand.

<br>

#### Hellfire Weapon
*1st-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 20 ft
- **Components:** S
- **Duration:** Instantaneous
- **Classes:**  Artificer, Warlock

You conjure a weapon made of hungering fire and hurl or strike with it. Make a ranged spell attack against a target within range, or a melee spell attack against a target within 5 feet of you. On a hit, the target takes 1d8 fire damage. If you score a critical hit or reduce a creature to 0 hit points with this attack, you can cast this spell again as a bonus action on this turn. After the attack is made, the weapon vanishes.

The spell’s damage increases by 1d8 when you reach certain levels: 2d8 at 5th level, 3d8 at 11th level, and 4d8 at 17th level.

#### Magmatic Stone
*3rd-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 100 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (A bit of igneous rock)
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Wizard

You conjure a molten rock and hurl it at a creature within range. Make a ranged spell attack against the target. On a hit, the target takes 3d8 bludgeoning damage. Whether the attack hits or misses, the rock explodes on impact, creating a 15-foot-radius sphere of whirling magma centered on the point of impact. The sphere lasts for the duration, and its area is lightly obscured and considered difficult terrain. The sphere spreads around corners and seeps through openings at least 5 feet in diameter.

When the sphere first appears, and at the start of each of your turns thereafter, it moves 10 feet in the direction you hurled it from. Any creature whose space the sphere enters or passes through must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, the creature takes 3d8 fire damage. On a successful save, the creature takes half as much damage.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 4th level or higher, the bludgeoning and fire damage both increase by 1d8 for each slot level above 3rd.

> ##### New Condition: Dazed 
> A dazed creature can’t take reactions and on its turn, it must choose whether it gets a move, an action, or a bonus action; it gets only one of the three.


##### Lore of Fel Dwarves Art Credit
* Nahiri's Lithoforming - Campbell White, Wizards of the Coast
* Fall of the Hammer - Adam Paquette, Wizards of the Coast
* Tormentor's Trident - Anthony Palumbo, Wizards of the Coast





\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

> ##### New Condition: Obsessed 
> The creature becomes fixated on a creature or object, which becomes a source of its obsession. Being obsessed has the following effects on a creature:
> * While the creature can see a source of its obsession, it can't target any creature or object with an attack, spell, or ability except for a source of its obsession.
> * While the creature can see a source of its obsession, it can't cast spells or use abilities that target an area (such as the  *fireball* spell) unless a source of its obsession is in that area. 
> *  The creature can't willingly move away from a source of its obsession.


#### Subjugation
*2th-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 ft
- **Components:** V
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard, Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard

You attempt to crush the will of one creature you can see within range. Constructs and undead are immune to this effect. The target must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or become frightened of you until the spell ends. While frightened in this way, the target is also charmed by you.

The frightened target can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself on a success.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 3rd level or higher, you can target one additional creature for each slot level above 2nd. The creatures must be within 30 feet of each other when you target them.

## Lore of Metal

This brand of magic specializes in manipulating metals and mechanical objects. It is favored by alchemists, artificers, and those specializing in transmutation magic. Spells from this lore can conjure metal for offensive and defensive purposes, alter the properties of objects to hinder their use, or even transmute creatures into gold. 

#### Commandment of Inertia

*3rd-level transmutation*

- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** Touch
- **Components:** V, S, M (A bit of glue)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 hour
- **Classes:**  Artificer

You touch a construct creature or an object with moving parts that weighs no more than 4,000 pounds and is no larger than a 20-foot cube. 

**Construct.** A construct targeted this way must make a Dexterity saving throw or be paralyzed for the duration. At the end of each of its turns, the target can make a Constitution saving throw. On a success, the spell ends on the target.

**Object.** An object targeted this way becomes jammed, and its internal parts are sealed together. For instance, a chest cannot be opened, a catapult cannot be fired, and a clock will stop turning. (If there is ever any doubt as to how an object will be impeded, imagine what would happen if glue were poured into all the crevices of the object; the spell should have the same effect.)


\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>



#### Final Transmutation

*9th-level transmutation*


- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (A bar of lead)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 10 minutes
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Wizard, Warlock
___

You speak a word of power that transforms a creature you can see within range. If the target has 150 hit points or fewer, it is petrified, turning to gold until the spell ends. Otherwise, the spell has no effect.

**Ending The Effect.** A petrified target can make a Constitution saving throw at the start of each your turns, ending the effect on a success. However, if a creature accumulates three failed saves against this spell, it remains petrified indefinitely until the condition is cured by other means.

**Effect On Other Creatures.** Any other creature that starts its turn within 60 feet of the petrified creature during the spell's duration must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or become obsessed* with the petrified creature until the start of its next turn. You can choose any number of creatures you can see to be immune to this effect.

**Damaging A Petrified Creature.** If a petrified creature is physically damaged or broken during this state, it will manifest the same damage upon being reverted to its original form.

**New Condition described at end of the section*

####  Hunting Hound

*5th-level conjuration*

- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 10 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (A golden whistle worth 100 gp)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 hour
- **Classes:**  Artificer, Ranger
___

Choose a creature that is familiar to you and that you have seen within the last hour. You then call forth a mechanical hound, which manifests in an unoccupied space that you can see within range. This **hunting hound** uses the stat block below. The hound is an ally to you and your companions. In combat, the hound shares your initiative count, but it takes its turn immediately after yours. The hound disappears when it drops to 0 hit points or when the spell ends.

**Detecting The Target.** The hound senses the direction to the chosen creature’s location and can see the creature as if it had truesight, as long as the creature is within 1,000 feet of the hound. If the creature is moving, the hound knows the direction of its movement. The hound cannot locate a creature if it is covered in or wearing wolfsbane.

**The Hound's Behavior.** On its turn, the hound moves towards the chosen creature, avoiding any damaging terrain. If it ends its movement more than 5 feet away from the chosen creature, the hound takes the Dash action, moving towards it. If it is within 5 feet of the chosen creature at the end of its movement, the hound takes the Attack action and attacks it. You can give limited commands to the hound (no action required by you) to slow down, stop, return to you, or continue its normal behavior.

If the hound cannot locate the creature, it returns to you. If the creature is dead, it sits by the creature’s remains and follows them if they are moved.

#### Law of Negation

*2nd-level transmutation*

- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (A nugget of fool's gold)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 10 minutes
- **Classes:**  Artificer, Cleric, Druid, Paladin, Ranger

Choose one non-wondrous magic item you can see within range. The properties and powers of that magic item are suppressed for the duration of the spell—for example, a +1 longsword functions as a nonmagical longsword. If the item is a potion or other consumable, it does nothing upon being consumed. An item under the effect of this spell still counts as a magic item for the purposes of other spells and abilities, such as the *disintegrate* spell.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 3rd level or higher, you can target one additional magic item for each slot level above 2nd. If you cast this spell using a spell slot of 7th level or higher, you may choose one wondrous magic item as one of your targets.

#### Metal Coat

*1st-level transmutation*

- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** Touch
- **Components:** V, S, M (a piece of gold thread)
- **Duration:** 8 hours
- **Classes:**  Artificer

You touch a willing creature who isn't wearing armor, and the creature becomes covered in a layer of metal until the spell ends. The target's base AC becomes 16, and it has disadvantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks. The spell ends if the target dons armor or if you dismiss the spell as an action.

#### Molten Silver

*5th-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 30 feet
- **Components:**  V S M (A small piece of sliver)
- **Duration:**  Instantaneous
- **Classes:**   Artificer
___

A line of searing liquid silver up to 30 feet long and 5 feet wide emanates from you in a direction you choose. At the end of the line, the silver spreads out into a 30-foot cone emanating in the direction of the line. Each creature in the line or cone must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 5d6 fire damage and 5d6 bludgeoning damage; on a successful save, the creature takes half as much damage.

#### Plague of Rust

*3rd-level transmutation*

- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (a piece of gold thread)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Artificer, Druid

You choose a creature with metal parts or a Medium or Small manufactured metal object weighing 80 pounds or less, such as a metal weapon, a suit of heavy or medium metal armor, or a metal door lock. A creature targeted by the spell can make a Constitution saving throw, ignoring the effects of the spell on a success.

An affected creature or object receives a -5 penalty to its AC, and any affected armor provides a -5 penalty to the AC it offers. Additionally, any weapon attacks made by an affected creature or using an affected object deal only half damage.

If you concentrate on this spell for the full duration, any nonmagical objects affected by the spell are destroyed, corroding into a pile of rust. A creature under the effects of the spell takes 3d6 necrotic damage at the end of each of its turns and makes a Constitution saving throw. The spell ends on the creature on a successful save.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 4th level or higher, you can target one additional creature or object for each slot level above 3rd. The targets must be within 30 feet of each other when you target them.



\columnbreak

#### Searing Shard

*1st -level conjuration*

- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 ft
- **Components:** S, M (A small piece of sliver)
- **Duration:**  1 round
- **Classes:**  Artificer

You send a sizzling jagged silver shard from your fingertips flying at one creature within range. Make a ranged spell attack against the target. On a hit, the target takes 2d4 piercing damage, and the shard embeds in the creature. At the end of the creature's next turn, it takes 2d10 fire damage if the shard is still embedded.

**Removing The Shard.** A creature within reach can use an action to perform a Wisdom (Medicine) check against your spell save DC to try to remove the shard. On a success, the shard is removed, and on a failure, the shard is still removed, but the creature takes 2d4 slashing damage.

**At Higher Levels.**  When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 2nd level or higher, the piercing and slashing damage each increase by 1d4, and the fire damage increases by 1d10 for each slot level above 1st.




#### Transmutation of Lead

*1st -level transmutation*

- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (A bit of lead)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 hour
- **Classes:**  Artificer

You choose a Medium or Small manufactured metal object that weighs 80 pounds or less, such as a metal weapon, a suit of heavy or medium metal armor, or a metal door lock. The object's weight is increased by up to 10 times your spellcasting ability modifier in pounds.

Additionally, a creature can no longer add its Dexterity modifier to attack and damage rolls made with the weapon. If the creature's Strength score is lower than your spell save DC, it has disadvantage on all attacks made with the weapon. If the targeted item is armor, its Strength requirement becomes equal to your spell save DC if it is lower.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 2nd level or higher, you can target one additional object for each slot level above 1st. The targets must be within 30 feet of each other when you target them.

## Lore of Shadow
This magic specializes in trickery, illusion, <br> and twisting the minds of its targets. Its <br> users primarily rely on illusory magic, though <br> they also wield spells that manipulate shadows <br> and even the nature of space and time as others <br> are able to perceive it, constantly leaving their <br> foes seconding guessing what they're seeing. <br> The following spells are examples of the types <br> of magic users of the Lore of Shadow often wield.

#### Creeping Strike 
*Evocation cantrip*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 10 feet
- **Components:** V S
- **Duration:** Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard
___

You lash out at an enemy with chilling shadows. <Br> Make a melee spell attack against the target. You <Br> have  advantage on the attack roll if the target is in <Br> darkness. On a hit, the target takes 1d8 cold damage.

***Cantrip Upgrade..*** The damage increases by 1d8 when you reach levels 5 (2d8), 11 (3d8), and 17 (4d8).

#### Mindrazors
*5th-level illusion*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 bonus action
- **Range:** 30 ft
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard, Warlock
___

You envelop up to three weapons you can see within range in phantasmal shadows, allowing them to slice through the minds of their targets. For the duration, when a creature is hit by an attack from one of these infused weapons, it takes an additional 1d12 psychic damage.

If a creature takes an action to examine one of the weapons and succeeds on an Intelligence (Investigation) check against your spell save DC, they discern the illusion and will no longer take the additional psychic damage from any of the infused weapons.

**Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot.** You can target one additional weapon for each spell slot level above 5.

#### Mirror Dance
*2nd-level conjuration*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 bonus action
- **Range:** Self 
- **Components:** S
- **Duration:** Instantaneous
- **Classes:**  Bard, Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard
___

You weave a shadowy link between yourself and a willing creature you can see within 30 feet, causing you and the creature to instantly swap places. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

> ##### The Quickened Condition
> A quickened creature gains an additional action on each of its turns. That action can be used only to take the Attack (one weapon attack or unarmed strike only), Dash, Disengage, Hide, or Use an Object action. The *haste* spell applies the quickened condition among its other effects, and a creature cannot benefit from the quickened condition from multiple sources at once.

<br>

The creature must be no more than one size category larger than you. The spell fails if either of you would appear in a space that cannot accommodate your size.

#### Mystifying Miasma
*2nd-level illusion*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 120 ft
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Ranger, Bard
___

You conjure a 20-foot-radius sphere of illusory fog at a point you choose within range. 

This miasma fills the air, spreading around corners and making the area heavily obscured for all creatures lacking true sight.

Any creature that starts its turn fully within the cloud must make a Wisdom saving throw. On a failed save, it uses its movement to travel in a random direction, determined by rolling a d8, until it exits the fog, after which it falls prone. The creature can then take the rest of its turn as normal.

**Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot.** the radius of the fog increases by 10 feet for each slot level above 2.

#### Penumbral Pendulum
*4th-level illusion*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 120 ft
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Wizard
___

You conjure a spectral pendulum that swings through a 60-foot-long, 5-foot-wide, and 5-foot-tall line of your choice within range. Each creature in this area can make a Dexterity or Intelligence saving throw (its choice). A creature takes 6d10 psychic damage on a failed save and no damage on a success.

At the end of each of your subsequent turns during the duration, the pendulum swings back from the opposite direction it swang last, repeating the effect across the same line each time.

**Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot.** The damage increases by 1d10 for each slot level above 4.

#### Pit of Shadows
*6th-level abjuration*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (A black cloth)
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Cleric, Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard
___

You conjure a portal to a shadowy plane, opening a 20-foot square pit on an area of the ground you can see within range. Creatures within this area must make a Dexterity saving  throw. On a failed save, a creature is banished to a realm of darkness for the duration. While in this realm, the creature is incapacitated.

At the end of each of its turns, the banished creature takes 4d6 psychic damage and must then make a Charisma saving throw. On a success, the spell ends for that creature. When the spell ends for a creature, it reappears in its original space or the nearest unoccupied space if its original space is occupied. If a creature dies while banished, its body remains in the shadow realm; however, any magical items it was wearing or carrying return to the original location.

**Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot.** the radius of the fog increases by 10 feet for each slot level above 2.

#### Shroud of Dusk
___
*1st-level evocation*
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** Self
- **Components:** V, M (A drop of pitch or piece of coal)
- **Duration:**  1 round
- **Classes:**   Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard
___

You release a surge of chilling shadows in a 20-foot-long, 10-foot-wide line that extends from you in a direction you choose. Each creature within the line must make a Constitution saving throw. Creatures take 1d10 cold damage, and on a failed save, and half as much on a success.

The line's area is then plunged into magical darkness until the end of your next turn. This darkness is impenetrable to darkvision and unaffected by nonmagical light sources.

**Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot.** The damage increases increases by 1d10 and the length of the line extends by an additional 10 for each slot level above 1.

Choose a willing creature you can see within range. The chosen creature becomes enveloped in a shroud of mist, enabling it to move with unseen swiftness. Until the start of your next turn, the creature's movement speed is doubled, it's quickened, and it becomes invisible along with everything it's wearing or carrying.

**Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot.** You can target one additional creature for each spell slot level above 3

*3rd-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 120 ft
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard
___

Choose a creature within range that can hear you. The target must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw, or its mind becomes filled with crippling doubt and inner turmoil. On a failed save, for the duration of the spell, the target has disadvantage on all checks and saving throws not triggered by this spell, and attack rolls against it have advantage. At the end of each of its turns, the target can make another Wisdom saving throw, ending the effects on a success.

**Using a Higher-Level Spell Slot.** You can target one additional creature for each spell slot level above 3.

# Fel Dwarf Forces

## Ashragoth Ironfist

Among the daemonsmith-prophets, none have ascended the ruthless hierarchy of the Infernal Priesthood or mastered the blasphemous arts of fel engineering as completely as Ashragoth Ironfist. The oldest living daemonsmith-prophet, he has ruled for centuries, his influence stretching across the fel dwarf empire like an unbreakable chain. His mastery of dark sorcery, malignant machinery, and fanatical devotion to the god of fire have made him a figure of absolute authority. His word is law, his will shaping every aspect of the empire’s relentless expansion.

Yet, for all the power and infamy Ashragoth has amassed, it has come at a terrible cost. Like all daemonsmiths who wield fiendish sorcery, he suffers from the Curse of Stone, a relentless affliction that petrifies his body with each act of dark magic. His limbs have stiffened, his once-boundless arcane might slowly fading. But rather than submit to fate, Ashragoth has turned his suffering into fuel for his ambition. He refuses to be a relic of the past. He will not just endure—he will conquer time itself.

To stave off his encroaching paralysis, Ashragoth has constructed a mechanical exoskeleton, grafting iron prosthetics onto his failing body. Now, he towers over his kin, his metal legs granting him inhuman mobility as he crushes those who dare oppose him beneath his ironbound feet. His mechanical arms, weapons of infernal design, enhance his lethality—one spews torrents of magical flame, turning all in its path to cinders, while the other wields a black-forged hammer burning with eternal heat, capable of melting through armor and shattering steel in a single blow. Even in his weakened state, his command of destructive sorcery remains terrifying, and entire settlements have been reduced to ash in mere minutes by the sorcery he commands.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br>

Now, Ashragoth moves the fel dwarf empire toward its most ambitious conquest yet. Raiding parties surge beyond the empire’s borders, bolstered by unholy warriors and infernal war engines. Cities fall beneath relentless sieges, their populations dragged away in droves to an unknown fate. Meanwhile, his most trusted agents—champions, enslaved monstrosities, and daemon-forged abominations—scour forgotten tombs and holy sites, seizing long-lost relics to fuel Ashragoth’s ultimate plan.

Back in the heartland of the fel dwarves, an industrial hellscape churns at an unfathomable pace. Mines are stripped bare, heedless of the countless lives spent in the process. Towering factories vomit thick, black smoke into a sky long bereft of sunlight, their forges never ceasing as they churn out esoteric devices of eldritch power. At the center of this chaos looms the Grand Black Tower, Ashragoth’s unholy citadel. Its presence grows stronger with each passing day, spreading a malignant aura across the land like an infection. The very earth quakes beneath it, magma seeping from widening fissures as nameless horrors claw their way from the abyss. It is as if the world itself protests the atrocities being wrought.

Yet, the true purpose of Ashragoth’s great industry remains shrouded in mystery. The few who have escaped his empire speak in hushed whispers of a monolithic device, a creation so blasphemous that all past infernal constructs pale in comparison. What Ashragoth intends to do with this unfathomable machine remains unknown. But one thing is certain—his ambition does not end with regaining his former power, nor even with complete dominion over the fel dwarf Empire. His gaze is fixed on something far greater.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/39nSBCzJ/Warchanter-Skald-2-Kaldheim-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-100px; right:-100px; width:1200px; transform:scalex(1);filter:opacity(100%);'/>

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:109px; right:60px; width:900px; transform:rotate(10deg)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:190px; right:0px; width:900px; transform:rotate(0deg)' />


\pagebreakNum


### Ashragoth's Lair
Ashragoth makes his lair in an obsidian tower located within a volcanic wasteland. Within the ziggurat, countless forges and altars are dedicated to the dark gods. The petrified bodies of former pupils and rivals of Ashragoth are embedded within the ramparts of the structure, At the heart of the temple lies Ashragoth’s personal laboratory, where he conducts his own dark experiments.

#### Lair Actions
When fighting within his lair, Ashragoth's Challenge Rating (CR) increases by 2.

When Ashragoth rolls initiative, his lair awakens to aid him. Until combat ends or the Ashragoth dies, the lair has an Intelligence of 20 and can act of its own accord, always acting in Ashragoth’s best interest. While active in this way, the lair is aware of the location of all creatures within it. On initiative count 20 (losing initiative ties), the lair can cause one of the following effects. It cannot use the same effect two rounds in a row:


**Seismic Tremors.** The lair chooses a 15-foot cube within itself, causing the ground in that area to violently shake. Each creature in the cube must make a DC 18 Dexterity saving throw or be knocked prone. If a creature fails the save by 5 or more (DC 13), it cannot stand up until initiative count 20 of the next round. The ground in the area becomes difficult terrain until cleared, and the tremors persist until initiative count 20 of the next round. At that point, the vibrations culminate in a calamitous burst, forcing all creatures in the area to make a DC 18 Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 21 (6d6) thunder damage. On a success, it takes half damage.

**Burning Souls.** The lair conjures a 10-foot-radius sphere of burning souls at a point within itself. On initiative count 20 of the next round, the sphere moves up to 30 feet toward the nearest creature before disappearing. Any creature in the sphere when it appears or that the sphere moves into must make a DC 18 Wisdom saving throw. On a failed save, the creature takes 10 (3d6) fire damage and is frightened until initiative count 20 of the next round. On a successful save, the creature takes half as much damage and is not frightened. If the creature fails the save by 5 or more (DC 13), it cannot take reactions and must use the Dash action on each of its turns to move away from the sphere by the safest available route.

#### Regional Effects
The area where Ashragoth dwells is corrupted by his presence, creating one or more of the following effects everywhere within 5 miles of his lair:
* While in his lair, Ashragoth knows the location of any petrified creatures. As an action, he can choose a petrified creature within this region. For as long as he maintains concentration, he can perceive and speak through the creature.
* Whenever a creature fails to pick a lock, the tools it was using are destroyed, and the creature takes 17 (5d6) fire damage.
* Fires cannot be extinguished except by magical means or by being doused in blood.
* Small earthquakes are common.
* Water sources within 5 miles of the lair are supernaturally warm and tainted with sulfur.
* Storms of hot ash are frequent.

These effects gradually dissipate over 1d10 days after Ashragoth's death.


##### Ashragoth Ironfist Adventure Hooks

| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Stolen Furnace:** A massive war machine meant for Ashragoth’s personal use has been stolen by a rogue fel dwarf warband. With both sides hunting them, the party is caught in a deadly conflict over a weapon that could change the course of an impending war.|
|  2  |**The Suspicious Defector:** A high-ranking fel dwarf engineer claims to have grown disillusioned with Ashragoth’s rule and offers to betray his master, promising blueprints to the Grand Black Tower’s infernal war machines. But is this an act of rebellion or a ploy by Ashragoth to lure his enemies into a deadly trap? |
|  3  | **The Devil’s Bargain:** Whispers tell of Ashragoth forging a dark pact with an ancient fiend to stave off his petrification. The devil now demands a price even Ashragoth refuses to pay. The fiend offers the party a chance to strike down the daemonsmith while he is vulnerable—but the cost of aiding such an entity may be even steeper.   |
|  4  | **Doom of the Mountains:** Ashragoth has ordered an entire mountain range mined out to fuel his empire’s endless war machines. The land itself rebels, earthquakes tearing through the region as something ancient stirs beneath. The party is hired to investigate before the fel -Dwarves unearth something that should have remained buried.  |

> ## Ashragoth Ironfist
> *Large construct (dwarf), lawful evil*  
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 18 (natural armor)  
> - **Hit Points** 420 (40d8 + 240)  
> - **Speed** 30 ft.  
> ___
> |STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
> |:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
> |20 (+5)|18 (+4)|22 (+6)|20 (+5)|18 (+4)|18 (+4)|
> ___
> - **Saving Throws** Intelligence +10, Wisdom +9, Charisma +9  
> - **Damage Immunities** poison, fire  
> - **Condition Immunities** charmed, exhaustion, frightened, paralyzed, petrified, poisoned  
> - **Skills** Arcana +10, Athletics +10, Land Vehicles +5, Smith's Tools +5, Tinker's Tools +5  
> - **Senses** darkvision 30 ft., passive Perception 14  
> - **Languages** Dwarvish, Infernal, Goblin, Orc  
> - **Challenge** 16 (15,000 XP)   &emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +5  
> ___
> 
> ***Consuming Sorcery.*** At the end of each turn, if the Ashragoth took 30 or more damage during that turn, he must make a Constitution saving throw with a DC equal to half the damage taken. <br>
> On a failed save, Ashragoth gains a level of petrification. After gaining three levels, the levels are removed, and one of his non-petrified limbs is petrified at random (see Limb Actions for descriptions of his limbs). Ashragoth gains a +1 bonus to AC for each petrified limb. If all his limbs become petrified, Ashragoth becomes petrified (ignoring its immunity) until freed by the *greater restoration* spell cast at 9th level.
> 
> ***Focused.*** Ashragoth's concentration can't be broken as a result of taking damage.
>
> ***Growing Malevolence.*** Ashragoth can concentrate on a number of spells simultaneously equal to the number of his petrified limbs. 
>
> ***Iron Will.*** If the Ashragoth fails a saving throw, he can choose to succeed instead and he gains level of petrification.
>
> ***Standing Leap.*** The Ashragoth's long jump is up to 30 feet and its high jump is up to 30 feet, with or without a running start.
> 
> ### Actions  
> 
> ***Slam.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +10 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 18 (3d8 + 5) bludgeoning damage.  
>
> ***Spellcasting.*** Ashragoth is a spellcaster. His spellcasting ability is Intelligence (spell save DC 17, +9 to hit with spell attacks). He knows the following spells:  
> **At will:** *guidance*, *mending*, *thaumaturgy*  
> **3rd level (3 slots):** *magmatic stone**  
**4th level (3 slots):** *fabricate*, *conflagration*, *wall of fire*  
> **5th level (2 slots):** *ash storm**, *burning head**, *commune*, *creation*<Br>
> **6th level (1 slots):** *divine hammer**<br>
>
>  **New spells described in the New Spells section*
> 
> ### Limb Actions  
> Ashragoth has three limbs: Harmer Arm, Scorcher Arm, and Piston Legs. Each limb rolls initiative at the start of combat using Ashragoth's initiative modifier and can act independently. A limb cannot use its actions if it is petrified or if Ashragoth is incapacitated.  
> 
> #### Hammer Arm Action  
> **Relentless Pounding.** Ashragoth moves up to 30 feet and then makes an Ashen Hammer attack. If Ashragoth has one petrified limb, he makes two attacks. With two petrified limbs, he makes three attacks.  
> 
> ***Ashen Hammer.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +10 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 7 (1d4 + 5) bludgeoning damage. Ashragoth can choose one of the following effects:  
> &#8226;  The target loses any resistance to fire damage until the end of Ashragoth's next turn, and immunity to fire is treated as resistance instead.  
> &#8226;  The target takes an additional 11 (2d10) fire damage.  
> 
> #### Scorcher Arm Action  
> **Infernal Wave.** Ashragoth moves up to 30 feet and releases fire in a 30-foot cone. Each creature in the area must make a DC 18 Dexterity saving throw, taking 9 (2d8) fire damage on a failed save or half as much on a successful one. For each petrified limb Ashragoth has, the cone's length increases by 30 feet and deals an additional 9 (2d8) fire damage.  
> 
> #### Piston Legs Action  
> **Cascade of Iron.** Ashragoth leaps up to 30 feet into the air and slams down into an unoccupied space within 30 feet, ignoring fall damage until the end of his turn. Each creature within 10 feet of the impact must make a DC 18 Strength saving throw. On a failure, a creature takes 9 (2d8) bludgeoning damage and is knocked prone. On a success, it takes half the damage and isn't knocked prone. With one petrified limb, Ashragoth can leap up to 60 feet, and prone targets can't stand unless they use all their movement. With two petrified limbs, it can leap up to 90 feet, and prone targets are dazed*  until the end of their next turn.
> 
> **New condition described at end of the section*

\pagebreakNum
  
### Epic Battle: Prophet of Flame
If you wish to turn the Ashragoth Ironfist into an endgame threat, make the following changes to his stats:

* Increase his Hit Points to 620.
* Change his Consuming Sorcery feature to require 5 levels of petrification before one of his limbs becomes petrified.
* Give him the Dark Father's Power feature descibed below
* Increase his Challenge Rating (CR) to 19.

***Dark Father's Power.*** Once per day, Ashragoth may cast the *eruption** (described in the New Spells section) using his spellcasting ability if he has two or more petrified limbs.



### Ashragoth Ironfist Tactics
Ashragoth's durability is immense, and he generally does not concern himself with taking damage unless it triggers his Consuming Sorcery ability. He only uses Iron Will if he is incapacitated or takes more than 60 damage on a failed save.

Ashragoth can take four actions per turn, which are divided as follows:



#### Limb Actions
* **Hammer Arm.** Prioritizes targets resistant to fire damage.
* **Scorcher Arm.** Aims for the most targets possible, prioritizing enemies with low Dexterity.
* **Piston Legs.** Used to reposition himself. He will seek to land near vulnerable targets such as spellcasters with low Strength. However, if he is close to petrification or low on health, he will use this to jump to safety instead.

\columnbreak

#### Spellcasting
Ashragoth uses his turn to cast spells. As more of his limbs petrify, he gains the ability to concentrate on multiple spells at once. He will attempt to maintain as many different spells as possible, casting them in the following priority order (1 being the highest, 6 the lowest):

**1. Divine Hammer** – Used if it can hit three or more targets. Ashragoth will position the hammer where the most vulnerable targets (those likely to fail their saves) will be directly underneath.

**2. Burning Head** – Placed between himself and enemies to prevent them from spreading out and avoiding his other spells.

**3. Ash Storm** – Used when he can hit at least three targets, or two targets with low Constitution.

**4. Wall of Fire** – Should divide the battlefield roughly in half while hitting at least two targets. Ashragoth can jump over the wall using Iron Cascade, forcing enemies to move through it to reach him.

**5. Conflagration** – Targets a creature with low Dexterity that is at least 30 feet away from any allies.

**6. Magmatic Stone** – Used when he can hit three or more targets, or at least two targets with low Dexterity.

#### Lair Actions

&emsp;**Seismic Tremors:** Use this ability to force opponents out of fortified positions and into unfavorable terrain, such as lava storms created by *magmatic stone* or the fire created by *wall of fire*.

**Burning Souls:** Target the players farthest from Ashragoth to pressure them into moving closer to him. Position the sphere to ensure they move toward Ashragoth, increasing the likelihood that they're forced into his reach.

### Ashragoth Ironfist Loot
Because fel dwarves are humanoids, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from them are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying or hiding nearby. Most dropped or hidden valuables can be found using **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Wisdom (Perception)** checks. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.



#### Ashragoth Ironfist Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

If you're running the epic Prophet of Flame version of Ashragoth, use the Prophet of Flame Loot Table to determine the additional valuables the players are able to loot.


##### Ashragoth Ironfist Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-9  | 2d4(5) 500gp Items |
|  10-12 | 1d6(3) 1,000gp Items | 
|  13-19 | 2d4(5) 1,000gp Items  |  
|  20-24 | 1d6(3) 2,000gp Items |  
|  25+ |  2d4(5) 2,000gp Items |  


##### Prophet of Flame Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-11  | 1d4(2) 5,000gp Items |
|  12-17 | 1 10,000gp Item | 
|  18-24 | 1d4(2) 10,000gp Items  |  
|  25-26 | 1d6(3) 10,000gp Items |  
|  27+ |  1 20,000gp Item |  

<br>

> ##### New Condition: Dazed 
> A dazed creature can’t take reactions and on its turn, it must choose whether it gets a move, an action, or a bonus action; it gets only one of the three.

\columnbreak

## Bull Centaurs
*Cruel Half-Bull Half-Dwarf Amalgams*<br>
**Habitat:** Desert, Grasslands, Mountain, Underdark, Urban, Volcanic; **Treasure:** Armaments <br>

Long ago, when hellish fiends first corrupted the forefathers of the fel dwarfs, they led them down a path of damnation. Some dwarfs, so thoroughly inundated with this insidious essence, had their resilient bodies and spirits utterly crushed. This unholy power fused their broken forms with savage aurochs, birthing the monstrous beings known as bull centaurs.

These nightmares possess the lower body of a muscular bovine and the upper half of a beastly dwarf, complete with large, curved horns jutting from their skulls. They embody the stubbornness and resilience of both bloodlines, combined with a fanatical devotion to the dark entities that fashioned them. Once roused to anger, bull centaurs are nearly unstoppable—hurtling forward with savage momentum, they slam into foes with horns, axes, and hooves, gouging, chopping, and pulverizing flesh.

Despite their massive bulk, bull centaurs strike with brutal precision. They often leave victims barely clinging to life, either to be devoured alive in ritual feasts or dragged to gore-soaked altars to be torn apart in sacrifice.
While some small tribes of bull centaurs roam the wastelands, butchering any they come across as offerings to their dark gods, most have been conscripted into the empires of the fel dwarfs. There, they serve the demon-smith prophets as elite guardians of the most malignant shrines and ziggurats of the dark gods. When the fel dwarfs march to war in great numbers, herds of bull centaurs often stampede at the vanguard, acting as terrifying shock cavalry.

Since their first emergence, only a handful of bull centaurs are born in each generation of fel dwarfs. These rare children are taken from birth and raised by the demon-smith prophets. Yet the limited number of these elite soldiers cannot satisfy the ambitions of their cruel masters.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

In pursuit of greater power, the demon-smiths employ their mastery of forbidden arts, seeking to twist their own children into more bull centaurs to swell their ranks. Most of these unnatural experiments end in agonizing death. Others are kept alive only through accursed concoctions, regularly injected to prolong their misbegotten lives, or through infernal prosthetics grafted onto their malformed, failing bodies.

<br>

> ##### New Condition: Resolute
> The creature stubbornly digs in to weather any assault. It experiences the following effects:
> * Attack rolls made against the creature have disadvantage.
> * The creature can't take its move action on its turn.
> * The creature makes Strength checks and all saving throws with advantage, except Dexterity saving throws, which it makes with disadvantage.
The Resolute condition ends if an effect moves the creature against its will, knocks it prone, or the creature becomes charmed, frightened, or incapacitated. A creature that is prone, charmed, frightened, or incapacitated can't become Resolute.


</span>

<img src='https://i.postimg.cc/L6xhTxxF/Stonebrow-EDHREC-1.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-0px; right:-130px; width:1070px; transform: scaleX(-1)' />

### Bull Centaur Warriors
Armed with massive axes and heavy shields, the rank of Warrior is the most common among their kind. Patrols of these Bull Centaurs can often be found guarding temples within the obsidian cities of the fel dwarves.

\columnbreak



### Bull Centaur Renders

More unruly than their brethren, bull centaur renders wield brutal twin axes. They hurl these weapons with ease at fleeing foes who manage to evade their crushing hooves.

### Bull Centaur Guardians
The most disciplined of all bull centaurs are trained to serve as personal bodyguards to the demon-smith prophets. Such is the fierce competition within the dark priesthood that no prophet of high standing can afford to be without these fearsome protectors—lest he be struck down by a jealous rival.


\columnbreak


___
___
> ## Bull Centaur Guardian

> ### Traits
>
> ***Debilitating Strikes.*** When the bull centaur reduces a creature to 0 hit points with an attack, that creature is Stunned for the next minute.
>
> ***Guardian Presence.*** While the bull centaur is Resolute*, each ally within 5 feet of it gains the benefits of three-quarters cover.
> 
> ### Actions
> ***Multiattack.*** The bull centaur makes two attacks, each with a different weapon.
>
> ***Battleaxe.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +8 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 14 (2d8 + 5) slashing damage.
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +8 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 14 (2d8 + 5) piercing damage. If the bull centaur moved at least 20 feet straight toward the target immediately before the hit, the target must succeed on a *Strength Saving Throw:* DC 16.  <br>
> *Failure:* The target is knocked prone.
> 
> ***Stomp.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +8 to hit, reach 5 ft., one Prone target or one two sizes smaller. *Hit:* 24 (3d12 + 5) bludgeoning damage.
>
> ### Bonus Actions
>
> ***Resolute Charge.*** At the start of its turn, bull centaur may move up to its speed in a straight line and become Resolute.
> 
> ### Reactions
> ***Pin Down.*** *Trigger:* A creature within 5 feet of the bull centaur stands up.
>
> *Response:* The bull centaur makes a Stomp attack with advantage against that creature. If the attack hits, the target fall prone again.
>
> **New condition described at the beginning of the document*
