### Bull Centaur Ravagers
Ravagers are more cruel than the rest of their savage kin. These sadistic creatures become intoxicated by the terror and panic they incite. With burning red eyes and ashen skin, they are avatars of horror. Foes who survive the initial charge often break into hysteria, fleeing in desperation—only to feel axes sink into their spines, leaving them helpless before the ravager’s insatiable, sadistic hunger.

\columnbreak

> ### Traits
>
> ***Debilitating Strikes.*** When the bull centaur reduces a creature to 0 hit points with an attack, that creature is Stunned for the next minute.
>
> ***Revel in Fear.*** The bull centaur scores a critical hit on a roll of 10–20 against frightened creatures.
> <br> <br> <br> 
> ### Actions
> ***Multiattack.*** The bull centaur makes one Gore and one Stomp attack. It can replace either attack with two Handaxe attacks.
> 
> ***Handaxe.*** *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack:* +8 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 20/60 ft., one target. *Hit:* 12 (2d6 + 5) slashing damage. The bull centaur does not suffer disadvantage on this attack if the target is prone.
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +8 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 14 (2d8 + 5) piercing damage. If the bull centaur moved at least 20 feet straight toward the target immediately before the hit, the target must succeed on a *Strength Saving Throw:* DC 16. <br> 
> *Failure:* The target is knocked prone.
>
> ***Overwhelming Stomp.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +8 to hit, reach 5 ft., one Prone creature or one two sizes smaller. *Hit:* 24 (3d12 + 5) bludgeoning damage and the target must succeed on a *Wisdom Saving Throw:* DC 16. <br> 
> *Failure:* The target is Frightened until the end of the bull centaur’s next turn. <br> 
> *Failure by 5+:* The Frightened creature also can't take reactions and must Dash away from the bull centaur by the safest route each turn.
> 
> ### Bonus Actions
> ***Resolute Charge.*** At the start of its turn, Bull Centaur may move up to its speed in a straight line and becomes Resolute*.
>

### Bull Centaur Khans
Those bull centaurs who possess the greatest cunning and might among their kind rise to become khans—also known as bull lords. These formidable specimens often lead herds of their kin, whether roaming the desolate wilderness or marching within the armies of the fel dwarves. At times, a khan serves directly under a powerful dwarven practitioner, acting as a trusted vassal and executing their master's will without question.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

When a khan charges headlong into battle to bring carnage and ruin to the front lines, the minions of darkness are quick to follow. Such stampedes shatter all opposition in their path, leaving only ruin in their wake.

> ***Multiattack.*** The bull centaur makes two attacks, each one with a different weapon.
>

>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +10 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 19 (3d8 + 6) piercing damage. If the bull centaur moved at least 20 feet straight toward the target immediately before the hit, the target must succeed on a *Strength Saving Throw:* DC 18. <br> 
> *Failure:* The target is knocked prone.
>
> ***Pulverizing Stomp.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +10 to hit, reach 5 ft., one Prone target or a creature two sizes smaller. *Hit:* 32 (4d12 + 6) bludgeoning damage. If the target is prone, the target can't stand until the end of its next turn unless it spends all its movement to make a DC 18 Constitution saving throw. On a success, it stands up.
> 
> ### Bonus Actions
> ***Resolute Charge.*** At the start of its turn, bull centaur may move up to its speed in a straight line and become Resolute*.
> 
> ***Stampede (1/Day).*** The bull centaur chooses a direction. It and any number of allies within 30 feet may use their reactions to move up to their speed in that direction in a straight line and then make one melee weapon attack. Creatures hit by attacks made this way have disadvantage on Strength and Dexterity saving throws until the end of the turn.
>
> **New condition described at the beginning of the document*

##### Bull Centaur Adventure Hooks
| d12  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Spawn Pit Uprising:** A fel dwarf fortress has gone dark, its forge fires cold and its gates sealed. Whispers speak of an experimental clutch of bull centaur progeny born all at once—mutated, unstable, and violently rebellious. The party is tasked with breaching the citadel to uncover what happened within, but the halls now belong to savage bull centaurs that no longer serve any master.|
| 2   |**The Sanguine Toll:** A remote village sits along an important mountain pass—now blocked by a band of bull centaurs who demand a grisly toll: the blood of one warrior per day, sacrificed at a gore-slick altar. The villagers beg for help, but the bull centaurs claim their offerings are holding something far worse at bay. Can the party stop them—or are the creatures telling the truth?  |
|  3  | **The Prophet’s Bodyguards:** A rising demon-smith prophet has sent emissaries offering terms of surrender to a border kingdom, backed by a show of strength: a pair of bull centaur guardians who now prowl the edges of enemy land. The kingdom hires the party to assassinate or neutralize these elite protectors before the prophet himself arrives to demand fealty—or deliver annihilation.   |
|  4  |**The Tainted Grove:** A sacred grove protected by druids has become twisted and toxic, its spirits slain or driven mad. At the center of the corruption stands a shattered altar repurposed by a band of bull centaur ravagers, who use it to offer grisly sacrifices to their gods. The party must cleanse the land—but slaying the bull centaurs may only anger the gods that empowered them.   |
|  5  |**The Broken Horn Khan:** A notorious bull centaur khan, once thought slain during a siege, has reappeared in the borderlands—now adorned with infernal prosthetics and leading a rogue warband. He no longer answers to the fel dwarves, and his rampages threaten both the empire and its enemies alike. The party is hired to hunt the khan before his forces become an uncontrollable tide of destruction.  |
|  6  |  **The Wandering Herd:** A nomadic tribe of bull centaurs has broken from fel dwarf control and now travels the badlands, seeking to reclaim ancient sites from before their transformation. They are hostile to outsiders but have knowledge of a sealed vault said to contain pre-fall dwarven artifacts. The party can choose to ally with, deceive, or fight the herd—each option leading to vastly different consequences.  |

\columnbreak

### Bull Centaur Tactics
#### Bull Centaur Warriors
If the warrior has a clear, straight path to an enemy, it will use its Resolute Charge. If no such path is available, it will stand its ground and fight enemies already in melee range (still using Resolute Charge without moving to gain the Resolute condition).
 
#### Bull Centaur Render
Renders are more adaptable than their kin. If denied a clear charge lane or if enemies keep disengaging, they will stand their ground and throw their twin axes at ranged targets.


#### Bull Centaur Guardian
Guardians typically operate in one of two roles:

**Personal Bodyguard:** Often assigned to protect a powerful spellcaster such as a deamonsmith, the guardian stays close to its charge to grant it its defensive aura. It may reposition itself with a charge if necessary to eliminate isolated threats.


**Group Anchor:** When guarding a formation of other bull centaurs, the guardian charges alongside them to ensure the group benefits from its defensive aura. The group holds formation unless disrupted by sustained area-of-effect attacks.


#### Bull Centaur Ravager
 Ravagers follow similar tactics to renders but prioritize attacking any enemy suffering from the Frightened condition.

#### Bull Centaur Khan
The khan opens combat with Stampede to shatter enemy front lines. Afterwards, it uses tactics similar to standard bull centaur warriors.

### Bull Centaur Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from bull centaurs are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying or hiding nearby. Most dropped or hidden valuables can be found using **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Wisdom (Perception)** checks. 

Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

##### Bull Centaur Warrior & Render Loot Table  (Avg. 28gp)


| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 3 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-4  | 1d6(3) 5gp Items |
|  5-7 | 2d4(5) 5gp Items | 
|  8-14 | 1d4(2) 10gp Items  |  
|  15-20 | 1d6(3) 10gp Items |  
|  21+ |  2d4(5) 10gp Items |

|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-6  | 1d4(2) 10gp Items |
|  7-9 | 1d6(3) 10gp Items | 
|  10-16 | 2d4(5) 10gp Items  |  
|  17-21 | 1d6(3) 20gp Items |  
|  22+ |  2d4(5) 20gp Items |  

##### Bull Centaur Khan Loot Table (Avg. 208gp)

|  24+ |  1d4(2) 200gp Items |  


#### Optional: Describing Looted Materials
If you’re not interested in the specifics, simply say the party collected materials worth the rolled gp value. If you want more detail, the tables below suggest materials for different gp values by creature. They also provide **Example Names** and **Quality Descriptors** for items worth **half** or **twice** the table's gp value.

For example, a 10gp Bone item from a bull centaur could be a Bull Centaur Horn, a 5gp version might be a Young Bull Centaur Horn, and a 20gp version could be an Elite Bull Centaur Horn.

***When To Use Descriptions.*** You can describe these items during looting, when selling them, or when crafting, but it's best not to make players track long descriptive names. Only use as much detail as is needed when needed.

\columnbreak

##### Bull Centaur Materials: 10gp 

|1d4 | Material | Example Name (Quality Descriptors) | 
|:--:|:---:|:-----------:|
| 1   | Bone|   Bull Centaur Horn (Young/Elite) | 
| 2   | Jewelry | Obsidian Insigina (Initiate's/Elite)|  
| 3-4   | Metal|  Bull Centaur Armor Plate (Inferior/Masterwork) |  

 

##### Bull Centaur Khan Materials: 100gp 

|1d4 | Material | Example Name (Quality Descriptors) | 
|:--:|:---:|:-----------:|
| 1   | Bone|   Bull Centaur Khan Horn (Damaged/Elite) | 
| 2   | Jewelry | Khan Insigina (Fresh/Veteran)|  
| 3-4   | Metal|  Khan's Armor Plate (Inferior/Masterwork) |  

#### Optional: Magic Loot for Item Crafting
If you plan to use harvested loot for crafting magic items, you can try to thematically align the effects of the magic items being crafted with the creature's they're harvested from. In the case of bull centaurs, Fiendish effects would make the most sense. These could be magic item effects that steal the lives of their victims or conjure unholy magic.

***Magic Loot GP Values.*** The value of magic ingredients depends on your crafting system. Subtract their cost from the normal loot’s gp value. If the ingredient is worth significantly more, subtract it from the next treasure hoard instead.



<br>

> ##### New Condition: Resolute
> The creature stubbornly digs in to weather any assault. It experiences the following effects:
> * Attack rolls made against the creature have disadvantage.
> * The creature can't take its move action on its turn.
> * The creature makes Strength checks and all saving throws with advantage, except Dexterity saving throws, which it makes with disadvantage.
The Resolute condition ends if an effect moves the creature against its will, knocks it prone, or the creature becomes charmed, frightened, or incapacitated. A creature that is prone, charmed, frightened, or incapacitated can't become Resolute.

<br>

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>


## Fel Dwarf Daemonsmiths

In the cruel nations of the fel dwarves, no position commands more influence, power, and reverence than that of the daemonsmith. These dark artisans are few in number, for only those who master fiendish sorcery, science, and earn the favor of the dark gods can attain such authority. The path to becoming a daemonsmith is as brutal as it is unforgiving. Ambitious apprentices subject themselves to the tutelage of a master, seeking to learn blasphemous knowledge. Most are deemed unworthy, and of those accepted, few survive the trials of apprenticeship. Many fall victim to their master’s wrath or the inherent hazards of their craft.

Even once an apprentice rises to the rank of daemonsmith, their position is far from secure. The hierarchy of daemonsmiths is a fractious one, with no singular leader. Each daemonsmith rules their own domain of servants and slaves, consolidating power through conquest, unholy pacts, or fealty to other daemonsmiths and fiendish entities. Yet, despite their pitiless nature, daemonsmiths revere the eldest among them—those who have survived for millennia and earned the title of daemonsmith-prophets. These ancient beings act as direct conduits to the dark gods and wield unparalleled sway within the priesthood's fractured hierarchy.

However, no amount of prestige can save a daemonsmith-prophet or daemonsmith who begins to show weakness. Products of such a ruthless system are terrifying indeed. They form the ruling class of the fel dwarf empires, dominating every aspect of society.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

Industry, war, law, and religion all fall under their iron grip. Through merciless ingenuity and singular authority, the fel dwarves have spread their empire unchallenged, constructing towering black fortresses of dark iron, inventing unholy siege engines, and crafting firearms imbued with fiendish power. Their insatiable thirst for dominance knows no moral restraint, as they enslave countless souls to toil in perilous mines or be sacrificed in malevolent rituals.

***On the Battlefield.*** The cunning intellect of the fel dwarves is no less formidable on the battlefield. They call upon terrifying magic to crack and scorch the earth, inspire unfathomable hatred in their allies, and sap the spirit of enemy forces, turning them into listless subordinates. Their mastery of machinery allows them to wield weapons of war with lethal precision, enhancing their destructive capabilities through potent sorcery.

Each daemonsmith arms themselves with the pinnacle of demonic engineering: blood-forged axes, black powder rifles infused with their very souls, and vials of molten liquid that can dissolve metal on contact. However, this immense power comes at a terrible cost. The dark magics they wield are dangerously unwieldy, and any lapse in control can result in a backlash of malignant energy that begins to petrify their bodies. Over time, repeated failures can turn a daemonsmith into a black granite statue, an eternal monument to their hubris.



<img src='https://i.postimg.cc/wTCWskg2/7350-hq.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-50px; right:0px; width:816px; transform:scalex(-1);filter:opacity(100%);'/>

##### Dark Forged Weapons

Daemonsmiths are masters of constructing hellish weapons. You may choose one of the following properties for each of the dwarf's weapons. (It has Dweomer Leach on its battle axe and Possessed on its pistol by default.)

##### Daemonsmith Weapon effects
| d6  | effect |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | ***Dweomer Leach.*** Creatures making Constitution saving throws to maintain concentration on a spell as a result of damage from this weapon have disadvantage on the saving throw. If a creature fails the save, the dwarf regains 5 hit points per level of the spell. |
|  2  | ***Fel Flare.***  The weapon deals an additional 7 (2d6) fire damage on a hit. Additionally, the target loses resistance to fire damage until the end of the dwarf’s next turn. |
|  3  | ***Life Bane.*** On a hit, the weapon curses the target. At the end of each of the cursed creature’s turns, it takes 7 (2d6) necrotic damage. The curse ends if the creature ends its turn more than 60 feet away from the dwarf, if the dwarf dies, or if the cursed creature regains 10 or more hit points. |
| 4 | ***Malignant.*** When the dwarf makes an attack against a creature, it can choose to become obsessed* with that creature until the end of its next turn. If it does, the attack deals an additional 10 (3d6) fire damage on a hit. |
|  5  | ***Possessed.*** The weapon deals additional 14 (4d6) necrotic damage on hit, if the dwarf misses or deals no damage on hit, it takes 7 necrotic damage as the weapon hungers for blood.
|  6  | ***Spell-Wrought.*** When the dwarf hits a creature with the weapon, it can channel magic into the attack, dealing an additional 14 (4d6) force damage. If it does, the dwarf has disadvantage on saving throws made to maintain concentration on its Curse of Stone ability until the end of its next turn. |


\columnbreak

##### Fel Dwarf Daemonsmith Adventure Hooks
| d6 | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Stolen Blueprint.** A young but ambitious fel dwarf daemonsmith has secretly constructed a siege weapon of devastating power—an experimental magma cannon capable of incinerating entire cities. However, the blueprints for the weapon have been stolen by a rival daemonsmith who plans to use them to gain favor with the dark gods. The party is hired—either by the desperate original creator or by one of the faction leaders fearful of this weapon—to infiltrate the rival's stronghold and retrieve or destroy the plans before they are put into production.|
|  2  |**The Petrified Prophet.** A daemonsmith-prophet of immense power has mysteriously succumbed to their final petrification, leaving behind a fortress filled with their unfinished creations, unstable experiments, and enslaved workers. The party is sent to investigate the fortress—either to claim the daemonsmith’s secrets, destroy the dangerous machinery left behind, or rescue survivors. However, the daemonsmith's spirit lingers in the cursed halls, manifesting through their machinery in an attempt to complete their work from beyond death.  |
|  3  | **The Master’s Wrath.** A fel dwarf daemonsmith's apprentice has fled their master’s forge, stealing a powerful artifact in the process. The master has sent mercenaries to recover the artifact and punish the apprentice, but the apprentice seeks refuge with the party or a nearby settlement, offering to share the artifact’s secrets in exchange for protection.   |
|  4  |**War of the Daemonsmiths.** Two rival daemonsmiths are locked in a deadly feud over resources, territory, and the favor of the dark gods. Each has fortified their strongholds with armies, war machines, and fiendish traps, and their conflict is devastating the surrounding lands. The party is caught in the middle of this brutal war and must navigate the conflict, choosing whether to align with one side, manipulate both for their own ends, or find a way to eliminate both daemonsmiths and their war machines.   |
|  5  |**The Breaking of the Chains.** A faction of slaves, including a number of brilliant but oppressed craftsmen, has revolted against their daemonsmith overlord and seized one of their war machines—a massive Iron Demon. The slaves seek to turn the machine against their oppressors, but the daemonsmith has sent their forces, including other war machines, to crush the rebellion.  |
|  6  |  **The Forgotten Outpost.** The players have been hired to explore and loot an abandoned fel dwarf outpost in the frozen north by one of its former guards. While looting the rusted remains and demonically possessed machinery, they encounter a daemonsmith and his retinue who've come to do some off-the-books looting of their own. |

> ## Fel Dwarf Daemonsmith Apprentice
> *Medium humanoid (dwarf), lawful evil*  
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 16 (chain mail)  
> - **Hit Points** 82 (11d8 + 33)  
> - **Speed** 25 ft.  
> ___
> |STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
> |:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
> |16 (+3)|8 (-1)|16 (+3)|16 (+3)|16 (+3)|16 (+3)|
> ___
> - **Saving Throws** Intelligence +5, Wisdom +5  
> - **Damage Resistances** poison, fire  
> - **Skills** Arcana +5, Athletics +5, Land Vehicles +2, Smith's Tools +2, Tinker's Tools +2  
> - **Senses** darkvision 30 ft., passive Perception 13  
> - **Languages** Dwarvish, Infernal, Goblin, Orc  
> - **Challenge** 4 (1,100 XP)   &emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +2  
> ___
>
> ***Battle Ready.*** When the dwarf makes a weapon attack, it uses its Intelligence modifier instead of Strength or Dexterity for the attack and damage rolls. Additionally, the dwarf may load a ranged weapon with the reload property when using its Resolute Stance feature (no action required).
>
> ***Curse of Stone.*** At the end of each turn, if the dwarf took 15 or more damage during that turn, it must make a Constitution saving throw with a DC equal to half the damage taken. <br>
> On a failed save, the dwarf gains a level of petrification. For each level of petrification it has, its speed is reduced by 5 feet, and its AC increases by 1. If the dwarf accumulates three or more levels of petrification, it becomes petrified. The dwarf remains petrified until freed by a greater restoration spell cast using a 9th-level spell slot.
>
> ***Dwarven Resilience.*** The dwarf has advantage on saving throws against poison.  
>
> ***Focused.*** The dwarf's concentration can't be broken as a result of taking damage.
> 
> ***Lore of Magic.*** The dwarf is specialized in one of the following lores of magic: Death, Fel Dwarves, Fire, Shadow, or Metal. The chosen lore determines one of its traits and the spells it knows.
> 
> ***Resolute Stance.*** At the start of the dwarf's turn, it can focus entirely on standing its ground mentally and physically. Until the start of its next turn, any attack roll made against the dwarf has disadvantage. Additionally, the dwarf makes Strength (Athletics) checks and all saving throws with advantage, except Dexterity saving throws, which it makes with disadvantage. The dwarf loses this benefit if an effect moves it against its will or knocks it prone. If the dwarf uses this feature, its speed becomes 0 until the end of the current turn.  
>
> ### Bonus Actions  
> 
> ***War Operator.*** When the dwarf casts a spell, uses the action station of a vehicle, or loads, preps, or fires a siege weapon, it can make one weapon attack.
>
> ### Actions  
> 
> ***Spellcasting.*** The dwarf is a spellcaster. Its spellcasting ability is Intelligence (spell save DC 13, +5 to hit with spell attacks). The spells the dwarf knows depend on the lore of magic it has specialized in, as described in its Lore of Magic trait.  
> 
> ***Dweomer Battleaxe.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 7 (1d8 + 3) slashing damage. Creatures making Constitution saving throws to maintain concentration on a spell as a result of damage from this weapon have disadvantage on the saving throw. If a creature fails the save, the dwarf regains 5 hit points per level of the spell.
> 
> ***Life Bane Pistol.*** *Ranged Weapon Attack:* +5 to hit, range 30/90 ft., one target. *Hit:* 10 (2d6 + 3) piercing plus 14 (4d6) necrotic damage on hit. If the dwarf misses or deals no damage on hit, it takes 7 necrotic damage as the weapon hungers for blood. If the dwarf made a ranged attack, it can’t do so again with this weapon until it loads it as an action or in place of an attack that’s part of an attack action. It can also load it when it uses its Resolute Stance feature (no action required).
> 
> ***Infuse Machine.*** The dwarf touches a willing construct, vehicle, or siege weapon and expends a spell slot. The target regains 19 (3d10 + 3) hit points, has advantage on its attack rolls, and imposes disadvantage on any saving throws forced by the target’s effects until the end of its next turn.
>


\pagebreakNum



### Fel Dwarf Daemonsmith Apprentice <Br> Lore of Magic Options 
Select one of the following lores or magic to determine a fel dwarf daemonsmith apprentice's additional passive trait and spell list. <Br>
**New Spells Found In New Spells Section*<Br>

> #### Fel Dwarf Apprentice: Lore of Death
>
> ##### **Death Trait:**
> ***Life Leech.*** Whenever a non-undead, non-construct creature fails a saving throw against or is hit by a spell attack from one of the dwarf's spells of 1st level or higher, the dwarf gets a +1 to its spell save DC and spell attack rolls for the next minute. It can only gain this bonus once per casting of a spell, and this bonus can stack up to 3 times (+3).
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *guidance,* *mending,* *thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1st level (2 slots):** *spirit leech** <br>
> **2nd level (2 slots):** *aspect of dread** <br>

<br>

> #### Fel Dwarf Apprentice: Lore of Fel Dwarves
>
> ##### **Fel Dwarf Trait:**
> ***Malevolent Power.*** The dwarf can concentrate on two spells simultaneously; while it is, it has a disadvantage on saving throws made for its Curse of Stone feature.
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *guidance,* *mending,* *thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1st level (2 slots):** *breath of hatred** <br>
> **2nd level (2 slots):** *subjugation**<br>

<br>

> #### Fel Dwarf Apprentice: Lore of Fire
>
> ##### **Fire Trait:**
> ***Kindleflame.*** When the dwarf deals fire damage to a creature with a spell, it gains a burn then takes 1d4 fire damage for each burn it has. The creature loses all burn after one minute of not receiving one.
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> **At will:** *guidance,* *mending,* *thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1st level (2 slots):** *hellish rebuke* <br>
> **2nd level (2 slots):** *scorching ray* <br>

> #### Fel Dwarf Apprentice: Lore of Metal
>
> ##### **Metal Trait:**
> ***Metalshifting.*** A creatures made of metal or wearing heavy or medium metal armor have disadvantage saving throws against spells cast by the dwarf, and the dwarf has advantage on spell attack rolls against them
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *guidance,* *mending,* *thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1st level (2 slots):** *searing shard** <br>
> **2nd level (2 slots):** *cloud of daggers* <br>


<br>

> #### Fel Dwarf Apprentice: Lore of Shadow
>
> ***Shadow Paths.*** When the dwarf casts a spell of 1st level or higher, it may use teleportation to swap places with a willing Small, Medium, or Large creature within 30 feet of it that it can see.
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *guidance,* *mending,* *thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1st level (2 slots):** *shroud of dusk** <br>
> **2nd level (2 slots):** *mystifying miasma** <br>

> 
> ***War Operator.*** When the dwarf casts a spell, uses the action station of a vehicle, or loads, preps, or fires a siege weapon, it can make one weapon attack.
> 
> ### Actions  
> 
> ***Spellcasting.*** The dwarf is a spellcaster. Its spellcasting ability is Intelligence (spell save DC 17, +9 to hit with spell attacks). The spells the dwarf knows depend on the lore of magic it has specialized in, as described in its Lore of Magic trait.  
> 
> ***Dweomer Battleaxe.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +7 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 9 (1d8 + 5) slashing damage. Creatures making Constitution saving throws to maintain concentration on a spell as a result of damage from this weapon have disadvantage on the saving throw. If a creature fails the save, the dwarf regains 5 hit points per level of the spell.
> 
> ***Life Bane Pistol.*** *Ranged Weapon Attack:* +7 to hit, range 30/90 ft., one target. *Hit:* 12 (2d6 + 5) piercing plus 14 (4d6) necrotic damage on hit. If the dwarf misses or deals no damage on hit, it takes 7 necrotic damage as the weapon hungers for blood. If the dwarf made a ranged attack, it can’t do so again with this weapon until it loads it as an action or in place of an attack that’s part of an attack action. It can also load it when it uses its Resolute Stance feature (no action required). 
> 
> ***Infuse Weapon.*** The dwarf touches a willing construct, vehicle, or siege weapon and expends a spell slot. The target regains 32 (5d10 + 5) hit points, has advantage on its attack rolls, and imposes disadvantage on any saving throws forced by its effects until the end of its next turn.

\pagebreakNum

It can only gain this bonus once per casting of a spell, and this bonus can stack up to 3 times (+3).

### Fel Dwarf Spell Casters Tactics

Fel dwarf spell casters adopt a resolute stance to establish a defensive position, often alongside other ranged attackers or siege weapons. They excel at lobbing spells and using either their pistols or infusing siege weapons. These spell casters do not retreat when engaged in melee combat unless they are overwhelmed, as their low speed and resolute stance improve survivability in close encounters.

#### Fel Dwarf Weapons
Fel dwarf weapons vary in effectiveness based on their type and the situation. The targeting strategy for each weapon is as follows:

**Dweomer Leech** – Targets enemy spell casters concentrating on spells.

**Fel Flare** – Prioritizes creatures with fire resistance.

**Life Ban** – Focuses on hitting as many distinct targets as possible.

**Malignant** – Best used against enemies attempting to engage the dwarf in melee combat.

**Possessed** – Targets the creature with the lowest AC in the group.

**Spell-Wrought** – Used whenever the dwarf has its resolute stance active to give it advantage on saving throws, canceling out the disadvantage from the weapon.

#### Lords of Magic

Fel dwarfs are intelligent and innately understand which spells to cast based on the situation. Spells are prioritized numerically, with 1 being the highest priority.

##### Lore of Death

&emsp; **Life Leech** – Works well with disposable minions, as they can be caught in the area of an AOE spell, enhancing spell effectiveness even if all enemies pass.

**Horrifying Laughter** – Cast on targets with low Wisdom saves, prioritizing the closest one.

**Wind of Death** – Used when it can hit two or more targets or a single target with a low Constitution save.

**Impending Doom** – Targets creatures benefiting from advantage (e.g., Barbarians with Reckless Attack or Rogues with Sneak Attack).

**Aspect of Dread** – Cast when it can frighten three or more targets, prioritizing clustered enemies.

**Crippling Pain** – Used on high-mobility skirmishers such as Monks or Rogues.

**Spirit Leech** – Cast on creatures with low Charisma.

##### Lore of Fel Dwarves

&emsp;**Malevolent Power** – If the dwarf is making four or more saving throws in a round or is one failure away from turning to stone, it drops concentration on its second spell.

**Divine Hammer** – Targets three or more creatures or two in the area where the hammer hits.

**Ash Storm** – Hits three or more targets or those with low Constitution saves.

**Curse of Stone** – Cast on targets with high health and low Constitution.

**Magmatic Stone** – Creates chokepoints or hits three or more enemies.

**Breath of Hatred** – Used to force enemies to focus on unfavorable targets, grant allies advantage, or keep an enemy from fleeing.

**Subjugate** – Targets martial classes directly threatening the dwarf.

##### Lore of Fire

&emsp;**Kindleflame** – The dwarf prioritizes spells against targets with burns.

**Burning Head** – Creates fear in enemies, putting the head between it and its enemies. The bonus action is used to slam the head into a target with burns.

**Burning Bolts** – Targets three or more enemies or two enemies with burns and low Dexterity.

**Wall of Fire** – Blocks enemy movement or hits three or more targets if it has already used Fireball.

**Fireball** – Targets three or more creatures or two with burns/low Dexterity.

**Scorching Ray** – All attacks should be stacked against one creature, as each bolt will apply a burn to the target. This is good for attempting to break concentration on an enemy spellcaster. For Sorcerer-Prophets, this becomes a priority if there is a target with three or more burns; the spell should be upcast to 3rd level.

**Hellish Rebuke** – Reserved for burned targets likely to hit the dwarf.

##### Lore of Shadow

&emsp;**Shadow Paths** – Enables the dwarf to swap positions with allies without breaking its stance, improving survivability.

**Pit of Shadows** – Targets three enemies or two with low Dexterity saves.

**Withering Resolve** – Cast on low Wisdom targets while maintaining concentration.

**Mindrazors** – Used when two or fewer creatures are trapped by Pit of Shadows.

**Penumbral Pendulum** – Targets enemies with low Dexterity and Intelligence or those affected by Withering Resolve.

**Mystifying Miasma** – Effective in chokepoints, hitting multiple enemies.

**Shroud of Dusk** – Cast when it benefits allies but used cautiously to avoid obstructing visibility.

##### Lore of Metal

&emsp;**Metalshifting** – Targets creatures in heavy armor or carrying powerful weapons.

**Blade Barrier** – Placed strategically to hit multiple enemies or block movement.

**Molten Silver** – Focuses on heavily armored enemies with low Dexterity.

**Vitriolic Sphere** – Hits groups or armored foes.

**Plague of Rust** – Weakens enemy armor. If the enemies have a powerful magic weapon such as a +2 weapon, it will target a weapon instead. If there are two or more such weapons being carried by the enemies, it will upcast the spell, making it a priority over 

**Cloud of Daggers** – Effective in narrow chokepoints or against clustered enemies.

\pagebreakNum


### Fel Dwarf Daemonsmith Loot
Because fel dwarves are humanoids, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from them are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying or hiding nearby. Most dropped or hidden valuables can be found using **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Wisdom (Perception)** checks. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Fel Dwarf Daemonsmith Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

|  8-10 | 1d4(2) 10gp Items | 
|  11-17 | 1d6(3) 10gp Items  |  
|  18-21 | 1d4(2) 20gp Items |  
|  22+ |  1d6(3) 20gp Items |

<br>

> ##### New Condition: Obsessed 
> The creature becomes fixated on a creature or object, which becomes a source of its obsession. Being obsessed has the following effects on a creature:
> * While the creature can see a source of its obsession, it can't target any creature or object with an attack, spell, or ability except for a source of its obsession.
> * While the creature can see a source of its obsession, it can't cast spells or use abilities that target an area (such as the  *fireball* spell) unless a source of its obsession is in that area. 
> *  The creature can't willingly move away from a source of its obsession.

<br>

## Fel Dwarf Engineers

Fel dwarf engineers are a formidable blend of craftsmen, artificers, and battle strategists. They are responsible for the creation and operation of the race's numerous war machines, including the fearsome Iron Demons and other infernal devices. These engineers view their creations not just as tools, but as manifestations of their veneration for the dark powers they serve. Their unique understanding of the arcane, the mechanical, and the fusion of the two make them exceptionally dangerous on and off the battlefield.

These enginneers possess an uncanny affinity for commanding the infernal spirits bound within their war machines. The construction and binding rituals are jealously guarded secrets, passed down through the generations in a complex tapestry of oral traditions and rune-etched schematics. They use their deep understanding of these forbidden arts to control and unleash their destructive creations with chilling precision.

When using fel dwarf war machines in your games, fel dwarf engineers are ideal for crewing and operating these devices. They will generally fight so long as their machines are operational and flee if they have no war machines on hand they can put to use.

## Fel Dwarf Soldiers

These soldiers are hardened, relentless warriors who form the backbone of the fel dwarf armies, carrying out the will of their dark masters with brutal efficiency. They are twisted fighters shaped by the same dark energies that have corrupted the rest of their kin, making them formidable and ruthless combatants. Clad in sinister armor and wielding weapons crafted from the darkest depths of their infernal forges, fel dwarf soldiers are a diabolic force capable of dominating nearly any foe they face.

On the battlefield, fel dwarves share the stubborn determination of their uncorrupted kin and can adopt resolute stances, allowing them to focus their entire being on withstanding the onslaught of their enemies. This unwavering resolve grants them an uncanny ability to shrug off most attacks and maintain their position, even under the fiercest assaults. However, this defensive posture comes at a cost, as it slows their movement and makes them vulnerable to attacks that require nimbleness to avoid.

The fel dwarf military forces are also known for their debilitating strikes that leave their enemies reeling from the sheer force of their blows. Even if their foes manage to regain their footing, the lingering effects of the strike leave them stunned and vulnerable. This combat technique is vital to the fel dwarves as it allows them to defeat their foes while leaving them alive for capture and enslavement.





\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>



> ##### Dwarves with Polarms
> Though dwarves in many fantasy settings traditionally use axes in combat, halberds, and other polearms weapons better complement the tactics dwarves use. Otherwise, they are vulnerable to foes who use reach weapons against them. If you wish to give the dwarves more well-rounded tactical options, you can replace their battle axes with halberds and replace their ***Shield Fighter*** trait with the following trait (only do this for dwarves with shields):<Br>
***Halberd Master.***  The dwarf can wield a halberd in one hand and a shield in the other.

<br>

Overall, these soldiers possess an array of combat skills and abilities that complement each other in combat. Some soldiers specialize in melee combat, wielding wicked axes, maces, or hammers with ruthless precision. Others excel at ranged combat, employing devastating firearms that can lay waste to their enemies from afar. Together they can form nearly unassailable military forces capable of laying waste to any who stand in the way of their implacable march towards conquest.

### Fel Dwarf Warriors

These soldiers are the mainstay of their armies, displaying unwavering loyalty and fierce determination in battle. They are often found on the front lines of fel dwarf forces, ready to face any foe with their cruel battleaxes and sturdy shields. The ring mail they don provides ample protection, while their shields are adorned with dread symbols of their dark allegiance. Like the warriors of their uncorrupted kin, they combine these masterfully crafted armaments with unyielding discipline to become a fighting force to be reckoned with.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

Despite being among the lowest-ranking dwarven soldiers in their armies, compared to the warriors of other races, these fel dwarves are still elite infantry. However, their combat prowess is offset by the relatively small population of their race. As such, fel dwarf warriors cannot be fielded in the same numbers as warriors of other races and must often rely on a mass fodder force of indentured soldiers to fill out their numbers. Because of this constant need for more cannon fodder, fel dwarf warriors often engage in raids to capture and conscript new soldiers for their army.

***Burning Beard Warriors.*** These fiery warriors are a rare and fearsome sect of battle-hardened fighters who have delved deep into the secrets of flame, harnessing its destructive power to rain havoc upon their enemies. They are easily recognized by their brass armaments and flaming hair and beards. The burning beards are specialized warriors often found in the ranks of the more ruthless and aggressive dwarf factions, using their mastery of flame to demoralize and devastate their foes.

Their prowess in battle is exemplified by their flaming battleaxes, which emit a searing heat that intensifies when either their target or the warrior is engulfed in flames. This fearsome power can turn the tide of battle as their foes are consumed by the relentless inferno.

When burning beard warriors are able to focus their fury in combat, it manifests as a surge of intense heat that erupts from their very being, igniting any who dare approach. The resulting firestorm serves as a potent deterrent to those who would dare to approach these formidable warriors.

Staying out of range of their attacks proves futile, for most of these dwarves are armed with sinister incendiary devices, which they hurl into crowds of enemies unleashing a devastating inferno that can turn the tide of battle in an instant. 

\columnbreak

> - **Senses** darkvision 30 ft., passive Perception 10
> - **Languages** Dwarvish
> - **Challenge** 2 (450 XP)
> - **Proficiency Bonus** +2
> ___
>
> ***Burning Fury.*** When the dwarf hits a target with a weapon attack, the weapon deals an extra 3 (1d6) fire damage if the target is on fire, and another 3 (1d6) fire damage if the dwarf is on fire.
>
> ***Burning Resolve.*** When the dwarf uses its Resolute feature, each creature and flammable object within 10 feet of it must make a DC 12 Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, the creature or object ignites in flames. Until a creature takes an action to douse the fire, the creature or object takes 3 (1d6) fire damage at the end of each of its turns.
>
> ***Debilitating Strikes.*** When the dwarf reduces a creature to 0 hit points with an attack, that creature is stunned for the next minute, even if it regains hit points.
>
> ***Dwarven Resilience.*** The dwarf has advantage on saving throws against poison.
>
> ***Resolute Stance.*** At the start of the dwarf's turn, it can focus entirely on standing its ground mentally and physically. Until the start of its next turn, any attack roll made against the dwarf has disadvantage. Additionally, the dwarf makes Strength (Athletics) checks and all saving throws with advantage, except Dexterity saving throws, which it makes with disadvantage. The dwarf loses this benefit if an effect moves it against its will or knocks it prone. If the dwarf uses this feature, its speed becomes 0 until the end of the current turn.
>
> ***Shield Fighter.*** While the dwarf is wielding a shield, its melee weapon attacks deal an extra 3 (1d6) damage when the dwarf hits with them (included in the attack).
> 
> ### Actions
> ***Battleaxe.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 10 (1d8 + 1d6 + 2) slashing damage plus 3 (1d6) fire damage if the target is on fire.
> 
> ***Naphtha Bomb (1/day).*** If the dwarf is not restrained or grappled, it hurls a bomb at a point it can see within 30 feet. The bomb detonates at this point, and each creature within 10 feet must make a DC 14 Dexterity saving throw. On a failure, a creature takes 10 (3d6) fire damage and ignites in flames (as described in Burning Resolve). On a success, a creature takes half as much damage and doesn't ignite. <br>
> When the dwarf attempts to throw the bomb, creatures can use their reaction to make attacks of opportunity against it as though it moved out of their reach. If a creature hits the dwarf this way, the dwarf drops the bomb, and it detonates at the dwarf's location.
>

### Fel Dwarf Blunderbussiers
Fel dwarf blunderbussiers are a terrifying <br> sight to behold on the battlefield. Known for their <br> distinctive, oversized firearms, these formidable <br> warriors unleash devastating volleys of fire and <br> shrapnel upon their enemies, their blunderbusses <br> roaring with the force of a miniature artillery <br> barrage.

Crafted in the dark forges of the fel <br> dwarves, these blunderbusses are marvels of <br> dark engineering, combining the dwarven <br> knack for craftsmanship with a cruel, destructive <br> intent. Larger and more potent than the firearms <br> wielded by their kin, these weapons are loaded <br> with a lethal mix of shot, black powder, and <br> arcane substances. When fired, they unleash a <br> devastating cone of destruction, capable of <br> decimating enemy ranks and piercing the <br> strongest armor.

In battle, the blunderbussiers typically form <br> the backbone of the fel Dwarf infantry, <br> positioned behind the ranks of shield-bearing <br> warriors. They unleash coordinated volleys at <br> the command of their overseers, turning tightly <br> packed enemy formations into charnel houses. <br> The sight and sound of their simultaneous discharge, a veritable wall of flame and death, is often enough to break the morale of all but the most steadfast enemies.






\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

But the blunderbussiers are not just marksmen; like all fel dwarves, they are more than capable of holding their own in close-quarters combat. When their blunderbusses are no longer of use, these dwarves can quickly don shields and draw axes to engage foes, and the blunderbussiers are as fearsome and relentless as any of their kin when forced to fight hand-to-hand.

#### The Granite Gunmen
The granite gunmen represent the pinnacle of fel <br> dwarf marksmanship. An elite cadre of blunderbussiers, <br> they are renowned for their unerring accuracy and <br> ruthless precision. Each member of the granite gunmen <br> has honed their skills over decades, if not centuries, of unrelenting warfare, becoming master snipers capable <br> of picking off key targets even amidst the chaotic <br> tumult of battle.

In battle, the granite gunmen are masters of <br> suppressing enemy movement with their precision <br> shots. They focus their fire on key enemy units or <br> individuals, disrupting their movements and forcing <br> them to take cover. The sight of a granite gunman lining <br> up a shot is enough to make any warrior think twice <br> before advancing, such is their fearsome reputation.

The granite gunmen often serves as the personal bodyguards to fel dwarf overseers, providing them <br> with a formidable defensive line. Their ability to slow <br> and disrupt enemy forces proves invaluable in protecting their charges, making them a vital component of any <br> fel dwarf force.
To become a member of the granite gunmen is a great honor, and only the most skilled and dedicated blunderbussiers are considered for this prestigious role. These individuals undergo a grueling selection process, during which they must prove their mettle in a series of trials that test their skill, patience, and resolve.

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

### Infernal Vanguard

The warriors represent an elite cadre of fel dwarf soldiers in service of their dark masters. These fearsome warriors are bound together by a shared history of past failures, which they seek to atone for through unwavering loyalty, unmatched ferocity, and the merciless conquest of their enemies. The path of the infernal vanguard is one of redemption and suffering, as each member dons an iron mask that obscures their visage, a symbol of their shame and a constant reminder of the debts they must repay.

The iron masks serve not only as a sign of their penance but also as a tool of dehumanization, stripping the infernal vanguard of their individuality and forging them into a single, cohesive unit. Beneath these forbidding masks, the infernal vanguard finds solace in their shared purpose and the brutal path toward atonement they have been provided. In battle, these masks instill fear in the hearts of their enemies, as they come to understand that they face an adversary that is relentless, unforgiving, and without mercy.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

In their quest for redemption, the infernal <br> vanguard is often tasked with carrying out the most <br> dangerous and brutal missions for their dark masters. From leading daring assaults on heavily fortified strongholds to hunting down powerful adversaries deep within enemy territory, the infernal vanguard willingly accepts any challenge, no matter the odds or the cost. For these warriors, each successful mission brings them one step closer to absolution and the eventual removal of their iron masks, a moment of triumph that few among their ranks will ever know.

Encountering the infernal vanguard on the battlefield is a harrowing experience, as their foes must face not only the formidable prowess of these elite warriors but also the relentless determination that drives them. The infernal vanguard will stop at nothing to achieve their objectives and atone for their past failures, and those who stand in their way must be prepared to face the full fury of their wrath.


___

***Fireglaivadiers.*** Among the ranks of the infernal vanguard, those who are chosen to bear the fire glaives are regarded with a mixture of awe and dread. These fireglaivadiers, as they are known, represent the perfect union of martial prowess and inventive savagery that is the hallmark of the fel dwarves.

Donning their iron masks of atonement, each fireglaivadiers is handpicked for their skill, strength, and utter ruthlessness in battle. They are trained to master the Fire Glaive, a weapon as dangerous to its wielder as it is to the enemy if not handled with the utmost care. 


\columnbreak

Yet, these warriors wield their deadly tools with a seemingly effortless grace, shifting between devastating melee attacks and lethal ranged assaults as the tide of battle demands.

In battle, the fireglaivadiers form the vanguard of the fel dwarf armies, their flaming weapons carving swathes through the enemy ranks. Their presence on the battlefield is a sign of the fel dwarves' determination to achieve victory at any cost. For the fireglaivadiers do not merely fight – they annihilate, leaving nothing but scorched earth and burning wreckage in their wake.

### Infernal Hellsworn
The infernal hellsworn are the most elite members of the infernal vanguard, chosen for their unwavering loyalty, exceptional combat prowess, and unyielding devotion to the cause of their dark masters. Handpicked from the ranks of the infernal vanguard, these warriors are entrusted with the sacred duty of serving as personal soldiers and bodyguards for the highest-ranking fel dwarves, including sorcerer-priests, warlords, and other leaders of their dark society.

Throwable blasting charges are a signature weapon of the infernal hellsworn, a testament to the deadly ingenuity of the fel dwarves. Forged in the dark, magma-filled foundries deep within their subterranean strongholds, these compact and potent explosives combine alchemical prowess with the lethal cunning of their creators. The charges contain a highly volatile concoction of volatile minerals and arcane substances, carefully encased within a rugged iron shell. When hurled at enemies, the blasting charges detonate with devastating force, unleashing a searing wave of flame and shrapnel that can tear through flesh and armor alike.

In their role as protectors of the highest-ranking fel dwarves, the infernal hellsworn are expected to be ever-vigilant, anticipating and neutralizing any threat to their charges before it can manifest. Their keen senses, honed by years of brutal training and the harsh lessons of their past failures, enable them to detect the subtlest signs of danger, allowing them to react with lightning speed to counter any would-be assassins or saboteurs.

***The Immortals.*** The Immortals are a legendary regiment of infernal hellsworn, renowned throughout the realms for their seemingly inhuman resilience and unwavering loyalty. Handpicked from the most elite and battle-hardened warriors among the infernal hellsworn, The Immortals are a force to be reckoned with on the battlefield. They are the epitome of dedication, forged in the fires of combat and tempered by the unyielding will to safeguard their masters at all costs.

The Immortals' extraordinary ability to endure staggering amounts of punishment is a testament to their mastery of both martial and arcane arts. Through rigorous training and dark rituals, they have learned to harness the very essence of the infernal fires that burn within them, channeling it into an unbreakable determination. This otherworldly resilience allows them to endure seemingly endless amounts of attacks that would fell lesser warriors, so long as the damage inflicted does not overwhelm them all at once.

\columnbreak

<Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br><Br>

In addition to their remarkable durability, The Immortals are known for their unwavering discipline and coordination in battle. They fight as a single, cohesive unit, each warrior's movements perfectly synchronized with those of their comrades, allowing them to respond to any threat with deadly precision and efficiency. This ironclad unity, born from countless battles fought side by side, enables The Immortals to hold the line against even the most overwhelming odds, defiantly facing down their enemies as a seemingly unbreakable wall of steel and flame.

The Immortals' legendary status has earned them the respect and fear of friend and foe alike. They are often called upon to spearhead the most crucial and dangerous missions, whether it be leading a desperate charge against an enemy stronghold or holding the line against an unstoppable tide of foes. Their presence on the battlefield is a rallying point for their  brethren and a harbinger of doom for their enemies.


___

> ***Burning Weapons.*** The dwarf’s weapon attacks are magical and deal an extra 9 (2d8) fire damage (included in the attack).

>

>
> ***Dwarven Resilience.*** The dwarf has advantage on saving throws against poison.
>

Until the start of its next turn, any attack roll made against the dwarf has disadvantage. Additionally, the dwarf makes Strength (Athletics) checks and all saving throws with advantage, except Dexterity saving throws, which it makes with disadvantage. The dwarf loses this benefit if an effect moves it against its will or knocks it prone. If the dwarf uses this feature, its speed becomes 0 until the end of the current turn.
>
> ***Undying Will.*** While the dwarf has 60 or more hit points, its Resolute Stance feature does not reduce its speed to 0, and it gains 25 temporary hit points at the start of each of its turns.

### Overseers

Fel dwarf overseers are a distinct and influential caste within their dark society, serving as both slave masters and military generals. These cunning and ruthless individuals wield tremendous power and authority, overseeing the vast legions of slaves and lesser fel dwarves that toil in the name of their malevolent masters.

As slave masters, fel dwarf overseers are responsible for maintaining order and productivity within the sprawling slave workforce that fuels their dark empire. They are masters of manipulation and control, employing a combination of fear, brutality, and martial prowess to keep their thralls in line. In addition to the physical and psychological torment they inflict upon their captives, overseers use their unyielding authority and presence to ensure the unwavering obedience and submission of their slaves.

In their capacity as military generals, fel dwarf overseers are tasked with leading the armies of their dark masters into battle. They are shrewd tacticians and skilled commanders, well-versed in the arts of war and the unique capabilities of their diverse troops. From the disciplined ranks of the infernal vanguard to the rampaging hordes of enslaved creatures, the overseers expertly marshal these forces to achieve their masters' objectives with brutal efficiency.

### Castellans

In the war-bent hierarchy of the fel dwarves, the castellans stand as towering figures of ruthless authority and raw power. These formidable warriors are chosen from the ranks of the infernal ironsword, singled out for their exceptional skill, tactical acumen, and the unyielding force of their will. Clad in the heaviest of armors and wielding their master-crafted fire glaives, the castellans are a sight to both inspire their allies and strike dread into their foes.

The castellans are more than mere captains. They are the embodiment of the fel dwarves' will to dominate, their relentless determination made manifest. Each castellan leads by fearsome example, plunging into the thickest of the melee or holding the line against overwhelming odds. Their presence on the battlefield is a rallying point for their kin, a beacon of unyielding defiance amidst the chaos of battle.

Castellans are bestowed with an ability unique to their rank – the power to infuse their underlings with a burning hatred that fuels their ferocity in battle. This hatred, shaped by the castellan's potent will, ignites their weapons with unholy flame, lending a fiery edge to their every strike. This fearsome power, combined with the castellan's own martial prowess, often turns the tide of battle in favor of the fel dwarves.

In their hands, the fire glaive is not just a weapon, but an instrument of inventive destruction. Castellans use special ammunition to maximize the havoc they wreak upon their enemies. Their molten bullets are not mere projectiles, but searing globes of liquid fire that embed themselves into their targets, burning them from the inside out in a spectacle of gruesome devastation. Even more fearsome are their exploding infernal slugs – projectiles filled with a volatile mixture that detonates upon impact, causing widespread carnage.


___
___

> ***Dwarven Resilience.*** The dwarf has advantage on saving throws against poison.

>
> ***Dig In.*** While the dwarf is in a Resolute Stance, it has resistance to all damage from ranged attacks, and its attack rolls with ranged weapons ignore half and three-quarters cover and don’t suffer disadvantage while attacking at a long range.
>
> ***Resolute Fire.*** While the dwarf is using its Resolute Stance, being within 5 feet of an enemy doesn’t impose disadvantage on its ranged attack rolls with weapons.
>
> ***Resolute Stance.*** At the start of the dwarf's turn, it can focus entirely on standing its ground mentally and physically. Until the start of its next turn, any attack roll made against the dwarf has disadvantage. Additionally, the dwarf makes Strength (Athletics) checks and all saving throws with advantage, except Dexterity saving throws, which it makes with disadvantage. The dwarf loses this benefit if an effect moves it against its will or knocks it prone. If the dwarf uses this feature, its speed becomes 0 until the end of the current turn.
>

If an attack with this bullet hits a creature, the bullet from the weapon becomes embedded in the target for the next minute. While the bullet is embedded, the creature can't regain hit points, and at the end of each of its turns, it takes 11 (2d10) fire damage. <br>
>  The target creature or a creature within 5 feet of it can use an action to make a DC 14 Wisdom (Medicine) check to attempt to remove the bullet. The target creature has disadvantage on the check to remove the bullet from itself. On a success, the bullet is removed, and on a failure, the creature takes 11 (2d10) fire damage.
>
> ***Infernal Slug (3/day).*** When the dwarf loads its fire glaive, it may choose to load it with an infernal slug. When the dwarf makes a ranged weapon attack using this slug, the slug explodes at the target location, regardless of whether it hits or misses the target. The target and each creature within 10 feet of it must succeed on a DC 14 Dexterity saving throw or take 11 (2d10) fire damage. A creature hit by the attack has disadvantage on the saving throw.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The dwarf makes two attacks.
>
> ***Fire Glaive.*** *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 10 ft. or range 100/400 ft., one target. *Hit:* 8 (1d10  + 3) piercing damage. If it was a ranged attack, it deals an additional 5 (1d10) fire damage. If the dwarf made a ranged attack, it can’t do so again with this weapon until it loads it as an action or in place of an attack that’s part of an attack action. It can also load it when it uses its Resolute Stance feature (no action required).
>
> ### Bonus Actions
>
> ***Infusion of Hatred (3/day).*** The dwarf chooses one other creature it can see within 30 feet of it and infuses it with hatred for the next minute. While infused this way, the first time the creature hits with an attack each turn, it deals additional 5 (1d10) fire damage.
>

##### Fel Dwarf Infantry Adventure Hooks
| d12  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Burning Mines:** The local mines have been overrun by fel dwarves, who have enslaved the miners and are using them to dig for a rare ore that fuels their infernal weapons. The party is tasked with freeing the miners and stopping the fel dwarves before they can unearth a vein of this volatile ore.|
|  2  |**The Hellsworn's Oath:** The party comes across a dying Infernal Hellsworn who, in a moment of clarity, reveals that he has been guarding a powerful artifact in a hidden fortress. The party must penetrate the fortress, dealing with other fel dwarves who are not so repentant, and secure the artifact before it can be used to bring about a catastrophic event.  |
|  3  | **Burning Vengeance:** A small town has been razed by Fel Dwarf Burning Beard Warriors seeking revenge on a local hero who foiled their plans in the past. The party must track down the Burning Beard Warriors and bring an end to the cycle of violence.   |
|  4  |**The Sniper's Mark:** A high-ranking official has been assassinated by a granite gunman sniper from an incredibly long range. The party must investigate the murder, identify the sniper, and find out why the official was marked for death before the next shot is fired.   |
|  5  |**The Immortals' Return:** Rumors are spreading of a legendary regiment of Infernal Hellsworn known as The Immortals returning from a century-long exile. Sightings of these seemingly invincible warriors have local settlements living in fear. The party must uncover the truth behind these rumors and prepare for the worst if they are true.  |
|  6  |  **The Castellan's Gambit:** A ruthless Fel Dwarf Castellan has captured a strategic fort, threatening to cut off a vital supply route. The party must infiltrate the fort, overcome the Castellan's forces, and reclaim the stronghold before it's too late.  |

### Fel Dwarf Soldier Loot
Because fel dwarves are humanoids, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from them are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying or hiding nearby. Most dropped or hidden valuables can be found using **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Wisdom (Perception)** checks. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Fel Dwarf Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

### Fel Dwarf Infantry Tactics
Fel dwarfs are twisted versions of regular dwarves who possess perverted versions of traditional dwarven traits. Dwarven stubbornness has turned to unrelenting hatred, their love of crafting has been channeled into the creation of weapons of destruction, and their pride now causes them to see all others as beneath them. 

Despite these grotesque changes in attitude, the combat tactics of fel dwarfs differ little from those of their standard kin. They are most effective when occupying a fortified position and using ranged weaponry to batter their enemies from afar while their unyielding melee forces hold the line.

One significant difference in combat strategy stems from their reliance on acquiring forced labor, as fel dwarf society runs on the backs of captured prisoners who are relentlessly worked to death. This means fel dwarves will not be content to drive an enemy off. If an enemy force flees, and the fel dwarves believe they have an overwhelming combat advantage, they will chase down their foes to capture them. 

There are two abilities common to all fel dwarves:

#### Resolute Stance

Dwarves can best use this ability when fighting in confined spaces that don’t require much movement. The optimal scenario involves a mix of ranged and melee dwarf combatants. The ranged dwarves will hunker down behind cover with this ability, making it very difficult to counter them with ranged attacks. They will then have melee dwarfs stand about 5 or 10 feet in front of them to stop anyone who approaches with readied attacks. Dwarves are patient and resilient, so they will tolerate taking fire from enemies this way if it seems like their own ranged attacks are outpacing their enemies’.

If the players bombard fel dwarves with area-of-effect attacks or effects that force saving throws, this may force dwarves out of their defensive position and cause them to charge the players or even flee if they’ve taken heavy damage. Though, many fel dwarves can resist common damage types such as poison and fire, which may allow them to better endure such abilities.

When dwarves use this ability, be sure to communicate it to the players. You can say something to the effect of “the dwarf plants his feet firmly and stares you down, ready for anything that comes at him.”

#### Debilitating Strike

The primary purpose of this ability is to allow fel dwarves to take prisoners of war to serve as forced labor. They will do non-lethal damage when bringing creatures down to 0 hit points, even if they’re fighting a group with a healer. 

#### Fel Dwarf Warriors

Fel Dwarf warriors act as the frontline in battle. When part of a well-balanced army, they generally use the standard fel dwarf tactics described earlier. However, if they are the only type of soldier on the battlefield, they will take one of two tactics depending on the situation.
* If the enemy can attack from range, the dwarfs charge into melee combat, taking the Dash action if needed to get within range. On their next turn, they will take a Resolute stance and fight, forcing their opponent to either fight them in melee with disadvantage or take an opportunity attack to withdraw.
* If the enemy charges the fel dwarf warriors, they will merely hold their position with Resolute Stance and ready attacks for when the enemy comes within reach.

Fel dwarf warriors prioritize attacking targets they can reach while in a Resolute Stance.

##### Burning Beard Warriors

When burning beards are on fire, their attacks deal more damage. Moreover, when they attack an enemy that is already on fire, it causes even more damage. Their main priority is to set as many enemies and other burning beards on fire. There are several ways to achieve this, including:
* If a burning beard is moving towards an enemy and can't quite reach them, they can throw a naphtha bomb that hits the enemy and themselves on the opposite edge of the blast radius.
* If a burning beard is in a resolute stance and doesn't want to move, it may use its naphtha bomb as described above.
* Running into a group of creatures using their burning resolve ability is also quite effective.

####  Blunderbussiers
Blunderbussier tactics are simpler than those of melee fel dwarf infantry, as they only need to find a good vantage point from which to enter a Resolute Srance and start blasting their foes. There are a few factors to keep in mind:
* The blunderbuss is a two-handed weapon, so the dwarf cannot hold a shield while using it.
* The Piercing Rounds ability means that the dwarf will prioritize targets with high AC but low health.
* After each attack with a blunderbuss, the dwarf must either use up its next action to reload it or enter a Resolute Stance at the start of its next turn, which will prevent it from moving. 
* If the dwarf cannot reload its blunderbuss effectively and is caught in melee combat, it will not hesitate to switch to a shield and axe to fight.

##### The Granite Gunmen
These soldiers are even more effective snipers than normal blunderbussiers, though they have no qualms about engaging isolated creatures in melee combat if need be.

One difference in their tactics stems from their Suppressing Fire ability, which makes them more likely to shoot targets that rely on speed, such as rogues.

#### Infernal Vanguards
These are elite dwarven soldiers that fight with unflinching resolve. Their tactics will depend on what they’re armed with.


\pagebreakNum



##### Axemen
These infernal vanguards are just a stronger version of fel dwarf warriors, with the only mechanical difference being that their attacks made with advantage hit even harder. Their tactics are essentially the same as normal fel dwarf warriors. 

##### Fireglaivadiers
Fireglaivadiers are unique in that they have a ranged attack but are more effective in melee combat. There are several attack sequences they can use:

When in a Resolute Stance with an enemy in melee range, they can make both a ranged attack and a melee attack. Since they don't suffer disadvantage from using ranged attacks in melee combat, this is the most effective attack pattern.

When in a Resolute Stance with no enemies nearby, they can only make a single ranged attack. This is useful when defending a position and waiting for enemies to come to them.

If the dwarf is close to a pursuing enemy or slowly retreating, they can make two melee attacks.

When trying to finish off fleeing targets, they can fire their weapon and use their other attack to reload. This is not an optimal attack pattern and should be avoided as possible.


#### Infernal Hellsworn
The main difference between infernal hellsworn and other fel dwarf infantry is their blasting charges. They will usually use their blasting charges when they are being charged, when charging toward an enemy, or if they can hit three or more targets. However, there are two things they must watch out for:

* Enemies within their reach can interrupt the grenade and cause it to detonate on top of the dwarf.
* When throwing the grenade, the dwarf must consider that other dwarves may be hit by the blast. Some dwarves are resistant to fire or outright immune in the case of the infernal ironguard. However, if dwarves caught in the blast are in a resolute stance, they will have disadvantage on the saving throw and likely take the full piercing damage from the blast. Depending on the circumstances, the infernal hellsworn may still opt to use the bombs even if they hit allies.

##### The Immortals
The signature ability of The Immortals is their Undying Will. It's important to note that they start the fight with extra temporary hit points granted by this ability. The Immortals typically begin the fight clustered together and try to bait out area-of-effect spells from the enemy, hoping that it won't deal enough damage to break their Undying Will, and they'll simply regain their lost temporary hit points. They may avoid this tactic if they know the enemy has area-of-effect spells that deal damage other than fire. Once The Immortals have spread out, they use their Undying Will to keep themselves safe while moving into prime positions. They prefer to fight one-on-one, as facing multiple enemies poses a greater risk of damage overcoming their Undying Will.

\columnbreak



#### Fel Dwarf Overseers
Fel dwarf overseers can make their allies more aggressive. They are most effective when the overseer has a mix of cheap expendable units, such as forced laborers and more elite dwarves and warriors.

##### Brutal Motivation
The overseer can use one of his attacks to kill one of his laborers to activate this ability. As long as at least two of his dwarves benefit from it, he will consider it a worthwhile tradeoff. The overseer can also trigger the ability by reducing an enemy to zero hit points, but this is a risky move and should only be done if he’s sure to bring the enemy down.

##### Harsh Discipline
The overseer sends non-dwarf laborers to slow down the enemy before using this ability on his dwarves and any laborers within range. This allows the laborers to better hold their ground and the dwarves to march forward and fight more effectively.

#### Fel Dwarf Castellans
Fel dwarf castellans share most of the techniques used by fireglaivadiers, with a couple of new abilities added to their arsenal:

##### Infusion of Hatred
This enhancement is placed on the most deadly dwarf under the castellan’s command who is not already benefiting from it, and it will use this bonus action every turn during combat. 

##### Specialized Ammunition
The castellan has two specialized bullets that it can fire from its fire glaive and will use them in different ways depending on the spacing of its opponents.

If its enemies are grouped up, it will use Infernal Slugs if it can affect three or more targets with the slug’s blast. Otherwise, it will use Molten Bullets on creatures that are either the most isolated from their allies or concentrating on spells. This can set up a deadly combo as party members attempt to assist each other with pulling out the Molten Bullets, while the castellan can take full advantage of them being near each other to pelt them with Infernal Slugs.


#### Dwarves With Polearms
The variant rule that allows dwarves to use halberds does not change their tactics but improves the already listed tactics, as having reach enables them to use their Resolute Stance more frequently. If you’re using this rule, keep in mind that it does remove the dwarves’ weakness to reach weapons. This is a more realistic tactical choice on their part, but it also gives players few options to counter them.

\pagebreakNum

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

## Fel Lammasus


Within the darkest reaches of the world, few monstrosities embody as dangerous a blend of bestial might and sorcerous cunning as the lammasu. With the hind legs of a bull and the forelegs of a lion, it sports two massive, leathery wings sprouting from its back. Its most striking feature, however, is its head—a grotesque visage of a male dwarf, warped with sharp teeth, glazed eyes, and a blazing orange beard and mane that blend seamlessly together.

Though the lammasu's sharp claws and long teeth, combined with its muscular body, can easily tear a man to pieces in seconds, it is the creature’s arcane nature and natural guile that one must truly fear. Lammasus wield powerful spells with ease, breathing in the winds of magic and exhaling faint, cold smoke saturated with dark sorcery. This miasmic cloud lingers around the creature, impeding spells that might otherwise end its life and smothering the enchantments of magical weapons and armor, rendering them no more effective than mundane tools.

Despite its lethal arsenal, the lammasu often avoids direct combat, preferring instead to manipulate others into furthering its vile machinations. Though its repulsive appearance might suggest otherwise, lammasus possess innate intelligence and charisma intertwined with their magical nature, allowing them to bend less clever creatures—such as wyverns, griffins, and even tribal humanoids to their will.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

Lammasus make their homes in places where the permeations of magic are strongest. Depending on the type of magic saturating a region, a lammasu's appearance and sorcery may be altered. Those dwelling in volcanic craters may have hellish red skin, obsidian claws, and the ability to summon gouts of fire to wash over their foes. Lammasus inhabiting tar pits, graveyards, or other places steeped in death often have gaunt, gray skin and pale white beards that fill mortals with an overwhelming dread of death itself. In the deep caverns and crevices where light is forsaken, lammasus stalk with panther-like coats and gleaming eyes, capable of twisting minds into knots and reducing victims to bewildered invalids. Meanwhile, those that claim abandoned factories or forges, once beacons of great industry, develop brass hides and metallic manes, transforming into monstrosities that can reduce masterwork weapons to cumbersome hunks of lead with a single breath.

Fel dwarves and other practitioners of forbidden arts prize lammasus as mounts of war, using their dark magics in tandem with the creature's own powers. However, while many who seek out a lammasu succeed in capturing one, it is often because the lammasu has deliberately allowed itself to be "tamed." In truth, it slowly manipulates its handler into unwittingly acting in its favor, eventually usurping the would-be master. Some individuals, however, are not so easily outwitted. This leads to a battle of wits between rider and mount, as each attempts to deceitfully bend the other to their will.

<img
src='https://i.postimg.cc/BnQpmYDb/Sphinx-of-Magosi-Art.jpg'
style='position:absolute;top:-40px;left:-70px;width:950px;transform: scaleX(1)' />
