\pagebreakNum

### Fel Lammasu Tactics
Fel lammasu are highly intelligent and cautious creatures. They avoid combat unless they have a clear advantage and will flee if threatened. Even when used as mounts, they act independently and in their own best interest.

Their typical strategy is to wait for enemies to group together before swooping in, attacking, and grappling a target to drag it away.

##### Lore of Death Lammasu
* Uses its *fear* spell to scatter enemies
* If a target becomes isolated, it launches a full attack, grapples, and flies away with them
* Uses *crippling breath* to weaken grouped enemies
* Finishes off wounded targets that escape with blight.

##### Lore of Fel Dwarves Lammasu
* Starts with *subjugating breath* to weaken foes
* Uses *magmatic stone* on grouped enemies (the lammasu is immune to fire and pursues foes through the flames)
* If enemies spread out, it grapples an isolated target
* Saves *curse of stone* for the highest HP foe who's not already debuffed

##### Lore of Fire Lammasu
* Uses Breath Weapon on enemies carrying metal weapons
* Weakens armor with *plague of rust*, then attacks and drags a target away
* Uses *searing shard* if its not grappling its chosen victim

\columnbreak

##### Lore of Shadow Lammasu
* Uses its Breath Weapon to scatter enemies
* Casts *withering resolve* on an isolated target, then follows up with *phantasmal killer* for a finishing blow



### Fel Lammasu Adventure Hooks
| d6 | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Lammasu’s Puppet.** A fel dwarf warlord has grown far more aggressive and successful, thanks to their mount—a fel lammasu. Unknown to all, the lammasu is the true mastermind, manipulating the warlord into gathering resources for its own mysterious goals. |
|  2  |**The Usurped Chieftain.** A savage tribe—such as orcish raiders—has been unusually strategic in its attacks. A cunning lammasu, posing as their spiritual leader, has secretly taken control, using them as pawns in its grander schemes.  |
|  3  | **The Lammasu’s Offer.** The party meets a lammasu willing to bargain instead of fight. It offers to help defeat a powerful foe if they assist it in reclaiming its “stolen throne” from a rival fel dwarf faction in a mountain fortress. |
|  4  |**The Lammasu’s Gambit.** A lammasu asks for the party’s help to escape its “captor,” a powerful fel dwarf lord using it as an advisor. The plea is a ruse, as the lammasu intends to overthrow the lord and take their place as ruler.    |

> ## Fel Lammasu
> *Large monstrosity, lawful evil*  
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 16 (natural armor)  
> - **Hit Points** 190 (20d10 + 80)  
> - **Speed** 40 ft., fly 60 ft.  
> ___
> |STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
> |:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
> |20 (+5)|16 (+3)|16 (+3)|14 (+2)|16 (+3)|18 (+4)|
> ___
> - **Damage Immunities** fire, necrotic  
> - **Skills** Animal Handling +7, Arcana +7, Deception +8, Intimidation +8, Insight +7, Perception +7  
> - **Senses** darkvision 120 ft., passive Perception 17  
> - **Languages** Abyssal, Dwarvish, Infernal, Undercommon 
> - **Challenge** 11 (7,200 XP)   &emsp;&emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +4  
> ___
> 
> ***Magic Resistance.*** The lammasu has advantage on saving throws against spells and other magical effects.  
> 
> ***Sorcerous Miasma.*** The lammasu emits a miasma in a 10-foot emanation. The properties and powers of magic items are suppressed while within the miasma. For example, a +1 longsword in the sphere functions as a nonmagical longsword. A magic weapon’s properties and powers are suppressed if it is used against a target in the miasma or wielded by an attacker in the miasma. If a magic weapon or piece of magic ammunition leaves the miasma (e.g., a magic arrow fired at a target outside the miasma), its magic properties cease to be suppressed as soon as it exits.  
> 
> ### Actions  
> 
> ***Multiattack.*** The lammasu makes two attacks: one with its Bite and one with its Claws. If both attacks hit the same target, the target is grappled (escape DC 17). Until this grapple ends, the lammasu cannot attack another target.  
> 
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +9 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 14 (2d8 + 5) piercing damage plus 9 (2d8) fire damage. If the target is prone, the attack deals 23 (4d8 + 5) piercing damage plus 18 (4d8) fire damage instead.  
> 
> ***Claw.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +9 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 10 (1d10 + 5) slashing damage plus 9 (2d8) fire damage. If the lammasu moved at least 10 feet straight toward the target immediately before the hit, the target must succeed on a DC 16 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone.  
> 
> ***Innate Spellcasting.*** The lammasu is a spellcaster. Its spellcasting ability is Charisma (spell save DC 16, +8 to hit with spell attacks). The spells and breath weapon the lammasu knows depend on the lore of magic it has specialized in, as described in its Lore of Magic trait. It requires no material components for its spells.  
> 
> ***Breath Weapon (Recharges on a Short or Long Rest).*** The lammasu exhales its breath weapon, as determined by its Lore of Magic.
>
> ### Bonus Actions  
> 
> ***War Caster.*** When the lammasu uses its action to cast a spell or use its Breath Weapon, it can make a claw attack.

### Fel Lammasu Lore of Magic Options 
Select one of the following lores or magic to determine a fel dwarf daemonsmith apprentice's additional passive trait and spell list. <Br>
**New Spells Found In New Spells Section*<Br>

> #### Fel Lammasu: Lore of Death
>
> ##### **Breath:**
> ***Crippling Breath.*** The lammasu exhales a black cloud in a 30-foot cone. Each creature in the area must make a Constitution saving throw or be wracked with pain. While wracked with pain, every time the creature takes a move, an action, a bonus action, or a reaction, it takes 9 (2d8) necrotic damage. The creature can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on a successful save.
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **1/Day:** *blight*, *fear*
>
> ---


> #### Fel Lammasu: Lore of Fel Dwarves
>
> ##### **Breath:**
> ***Subjugating Breath.*** The lammasu exhales a purple mist in a 30-foot cone. Each creature in the area must make a DC 16 Wisdom saving throw or be charmed and frightened of the lammasu. The creature can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on a successful save.
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **1/Day:** *curse of stone**, *magmatic stone**
>
> ---


> #### Fel Lammasu: Lore of Fire
>
> ##### **Breath:**
> ***Conflagrating Breath.*** The lammasu exhales fire in a 30-foot cone. Each creature in the area must make a DC 16 Dexterity saving throw or be set on fire. A burning target sheds bright light in a 30-foot radius and dim light for an additional 30 feet, and it can’t benefit from being invisible. At the end of each of its turns while on fire, the target takes 10 (4d4) fire damage. A creature can use its action to douse the fire by making a DC 16 Dexterity check. On a success, the flames are extinguished. The flames are also extinguished if the creature is fully submerged in water or standing in an area with strong wind (at least 20 miles per hour).
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **1/Day:** *fireball*, *wall of fire*
>
> ---


> #### Fel Lammasu: Lore of Metal
>
> ##### **Breath:**
> ***Breath of Transmutation.*** The lammasu exhales a breath that turns metal into lead in a 30-foot cone. Each Medium or Small manufactured metal object that weighs 80 pounds or less in the cone, such as a metal weapon, a suit of heavy or medium metal armor, or a metal door lock, has its weight increased by 40 pounds for 1 minute. Additionally, a creature can no longer add its Dexterity modifier to attack and damage rolls made with the weapon. If the creature's Strength score is lower than 16, it has disadvantage on all attacks made with the weapon. If the targeted item is armor, its Strength requirement becomes 16 if it is lower. A creature in the cone may make a DC 16 Dexterity saving throw to avoid having any object it is wearing or carrying be affected by the breath.
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **1/Day:** *plague of rust**, *searing shard** (5th level)
>
> ---


> #### Fel Lammasu: Lore of Shadow
>
> ##### **Breath:**
> ***Mystifying Breath.*** The lammasu exhales an illusory fog in a 30-foot cone. Each creature in the area must make a DC 16 Wisdom saving throw or be mystified. While mystified, the creature uses all its movement to travel in a random direction at the start of its turn, determined by rolling a d8. After moving, it can take the rest of its turn as normal. The creature can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on a successful save.
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **1/Day:** *phantasmal killer*, *withering resolve**
>

### Fel Lammasu Loot
The valuable items looted from lammasus will generally come from whatever can be harvested from them. This harvesting can usually be done using a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Arcana)** check. However, you may allow players proficient with specific tools to harvest items related to that tool. For example, a character might make a Wisdom (Leathworker’s Tools) check to harvest the hide or beard of a lammasu. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Fel Lammasu Loot Table
The following table describes the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

##### Fel Lammasu Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-10  | 2d4(5) 50gp Items |
|  11-16 | 2d4(5) 100gp Items | 
|  17-23 | 2d8(9) 100gp Items  |  
|  24-26 | 1d6(3) 1,000gp Items |  
|  27+ |  1d6(3) 2,000gp Items |

## Infernal Destroyers

These fiendish creations represent the pinnacle <br> of fel dwarf craftsmanship and their ability to <br> bind demons within machines. Infernal destroyers are massive constructs that stand as titanic embodiments <br> of the fel dwarves' irreverent audacity and relentless pursuit of power. Each infernal destroyer is unique, meticulously designed and crafted by the most skilled fel dwarf engineers and infusors, reflecting the personality, preferences, and ambitions of its creator.

During their creation, a grand ritual of binding is undertaken, calling forth a powerful demon spirit from the chaotic abyss and entrapping it within the cold iron of the construct. This demonic essence provides the machine with a sinister semblance of life and fuels its formidable abilities. The metal of an infernal destroyer is superheated by the trapped spirit, causing it to glow with a fearsome, otherworldly light and scorch the earth it walks upon.

Infernal destroyers can take a variety of forms, from hulking siege machines in the shape of bulls to monstrous constructs with draconic forms and flaming wings capable of decimating entire armies. The exact abilities of a destroyer vary with its form and purpose. Some might be fitted with massive armor, others might devastate their foes with an array of slashing blades across their body, and yet others may shatter foes with mighty charges and fiendish horns.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>



Despite their terrifying power, infernal destroyers are not without vulnerabilities. The fiery demon spirits that animate them are a volatile source of power, pushing the metal bodies of the constructs to their limits. If the destroyer has sustained heavy damage and continues to exert itself, the demonic energies within will begin tearing it apart and hindering its ability to operate. Should this process continue unchecked while the destroyer continues to fight, the volatile forces within will eventually destroy it from the inside out. 

Despite this weakness, infernal destroyers can typically win the day for their fel dwarf masters before collapsing. Their masters then quickly recover their remains so they can be repaired and reanimated for their next rampage.


<img src='https://i.ibb.co/FXbGKY8/minard-maxime-mtgburnishedhyenalowrez.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-85px; right:-640px; width:1500px; transform:rotate(0deg);filter:opacity(100%);'/>

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:450px; right:0px; width:920px; transform:rotate(0deg)' />

> ## Infernal Destroyer
> *Huge construct, lawful evil*

> - **Hit Points** 370 (20d20+120)
> - **Speed** 60 ft.

> - **Damage Resistances** cold, psychic; bludgeoning, piercing, and 
slashing from nonmagical attacks that aren't not made with adamantine 
 weapons
> - **Skills** Athletics +13
> - **Condition Immunities** charmed, exhaustion, frightened, paralyzed, petrified, poisoned
> - **Senses** passive Perception 13

> ___
>
> ***Blazing Body.*** At the end of the destroyer’s turn, each other creature within 10 feet of it takes 10 (3d6) fire damage. If the destroyer takes 5 or cold damage, this trait doesn't function at the end of the the destroyer’s next turn.
>
> ***Burning Bright.*** At the start of the destroyer's turn, if it has 280 or fewer hit points and took action on its last turn, it gains a level of Instability and takes 20 force damage for each level of Instability it has. It removes a level of Instability at the end of any turn if gained 20 more hit points that turn.
>
> ***Fire Absorption.*** Whenever destroyer is subjected to fire damage from source other then it's self, it takes no damage and instead regains a number of hit points equal to the fire damage dealt.
>
> ***Hell-Forged.*** The destroyer has the soul demon bound to within it. It counts as a fiend when determining the effects of features such as a paladin’s Divine Smite or a ranger’s Primeval Awareness.
>
> ***Immutable Form.*** The destroyer is immune to any spell or effect that would alter its form.
>
> ***Magic Resistance.*** The destroyer has advantage on saving throws against spells and other magical effects.
>
> ***Magic Weapons.*** The destroyer's weapon attacks are magical.
>
> ### Actions 
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The destroyer makes three attacks. It can replace one of these attacks with Burning Barrage. If the destroyer has two levels of Instability, it can only make two attacks. If it has four more levels of Instability, it can only make one attack.
>
> ***Slam.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +13 to hit, reach 15 ft., one target. *Hit:* 24 (3d10 + 8) bludgeoning damage plus 17 (5d6) fire damage.
>
> ***Burning Barrage.***  The destroyer lets loose bolts of fire at a point 15 to 60 feet away from itself. Each creature within 15 feet of the point must make a DC 19 Dexterity saving throw, taking 17 (5d6) fire damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/jWjR3Vw/Moltensteel-Dragon-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; bottom:-140px; right:-0px; width:830px; transform:rotate(0deg);filter:opacity(100%);'/>

\pagebreakNum


### Destroyer Enhancements
If you wish to create a more powerful version of the infernal destroyer, you can give it one of the following enhancements. Doing so increases its CR to 18.

#### Bovine Horns

*This destroyer has been forged in the likeness of a great bull, and if it picks up enough momentum, its horns can shatter mountains.*

When the destroyer makes a Slam attack, it deals extra 13 (2d12) piercing damage on hit for every 20 feet it moved straight toward the target before it hit. If the target is a creature, it must succeed on a DC 21 Strength saving throw or be pushed up to 20 feet away and knocked prone. If it fails the save by 5 or more (DC 16), it can't stand up until the start of the destroyer's next turn.

#### Blazing Wings

*The destroyer has been equipped with flaming wings capable of unleashing waves of fire when it lands on the ground.*

The destroyer has a fly speed of 60.

Additionally, if the destroyer is flying and dives at least 20 feet in a straight line before landing on the ground, each other creature standing on the ground within 10 feet of it must make a DC 21 Dexterity saving throw. A creature takes 9 (2d8) fire damage on a failed save and half as much damage on a successful one. 

For each additional 20 feet the destroyer dove before landing, the area of the effect increases by 10 feet, and the damage increases by 9 (2d8).

#### Colossal Plating

*The destroyer has been fitted with large black iron plates welded on either side of its body and etched with unholy runes, which render it nearly indestructible unless they can be removed.*

The destroyer starts with two iron plates attached to it. For each plate attached, it gets +3 to all saving throws and its AC (+6 while both are attached). A creature within 5 feet of the destroyer can use its action to make a DC 21 Strength check to detach one of the plates. It may add its proficiency bonus if it is proficient with Smith's Tools. The creature takes 10(3d6) fire damage when it makes the check if the destroyer's Blazing Body trait is active.

#### Gore Blades

*The destroyer’s body has been covered in razor-sharp blades capable of slicing apart any who draw near.*.

The destroyer's Slam now deals 29 (6d6 + 8) slashing damage plus 17 (5d6) fire damage on hit.

When a creature misses with a melee attack against the destroyer while within 5 feet of it, attempts to grapple it, or starts its turn grappling it, the creature takes 10 (3d6) slashing damage. 

Additionally, when a creature moves into or within the area the destroyer is occupying, the creature takes 10 (3d6) slashing damage for every 5 feet it travels.

\columnbreak

### Infernal Destroyer Loot
Because infernal destroyers are constructs, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from them are materials salvaged from their remains. Salvaged material can be gathered using an Intelligence (Arcana), Intelligence (Smith’s Tolls), or Intelligence (Tinker’s Tools) check. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Infernal Destroyer Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

|  19-23 | 1d6(3) 1,000gp Items & 4d6(14) 100gp Items | 
|  24+ | 1d4(2) 2,000gp Items & 3d6(10) 200gp Items |

### Infernal Destroyer Tactics

Infernal destroyers are mindless monsters, driven solely by their destructive instincts, with little regard for their own survival. They never flee from a fight and will fight to the death. However, their creators can guide their actions and may direct them to execute more complex tactics. If these creators are killed or incapacitated, the destroyer will revert back to its base instincts.

Infernal destroyers serve as hard-hitting shock troopers. Because their Burning Bright feature causes them to become unstable over time and lose attacks as they take damage, their best defense is their offense, hitting with such force that opponents struggle to properly retaliate from the brutal attacks. 

When guided by a more intelligent mind, they may attempt to engage the largest group of enemies to set them ablaze with their Blazing Body feature, focusing all attacks on any targets they believe will resist being burned away by their aura. They may unleash a 'Burning Barrage' to target backline foes, especially those casting dangerous spells. 

Armies with one or more infernal destroyers will follow similar tactics, aiming to hit hard at the beginning of the fight to break their enemies, utilizing all available resources and their strongest spells early in combat before their destroyers run the risk of destabilizing.

Infernal destroyers can be equipped with one of four upgrades that slightly alter their tactics:
* **Blazing Wings:** Allows them to disrupt backline foes by flying past sturdy front liners and slamming into groups of ranged combatants and spellcasters.

* **Colossal Plating:** Turns them into juggernauts, helping them stay alive. Their dwarven allies will focus on impeding whoever is most likely to remove the plating.

* **Gore Blades:** Enables them to shred through swarms of melee enemies, staying in the front line and serving as a blockade to protect more vulnerable creatures fighting alongside the destroyer.

* **Razer Horns:** Enhances their ability to destroy single targets. Fragile damage dealers, such as lightly armored wizards, will be decimated if the destroyer reaches them, and the destroyer is not afraid to take opportunity attacks if it means getting a charge against its intended target.


\pagebreakNum

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

## Infernal Fireborn
*Burning Demon Souls Bound To Servitude*<br>
**Habitat:** Desert, Mountain, Underdark, <br> Urban, Volcanic; **Treasure:** Armaments <br>


Fel dwarves possess an insatiable hunger for power <br> and a ferocious hatred for all beyond their own kind. <br> These traits have driven them to place no trust in, nor offer loyalty to, any being save themselves and their great and terrible gods—whom they follow only in the hope of stealing or coveting some portion of their blasphemous power.

So intense is the urge to dominate that burns within a fel dwarf’s black heart, the notion of serving another fiendish creature is both repugnant and insufferable. Thus, the deamonsmiths of their kind have spent lifetimes delving into the depths of sorcery and science, devising methods to bind and break hellish entities to their will. From this tireless research, the fireborn were brought into existence.

These living weapons of war are forged by fusing a bound demonic spirit into a volatile mixture of molten magma and the boiling blood of sacrificial victims. This unholy compound is then poured into cold bronze suits of armor, etched with countless incantations of binding. The result is a machine given a sinister semblance of life, its formidable abilities fueled by the demonic fire trapped within. The metal of an infernal fireborn glows with an otherworldly light, superheated by the spirit’s fury, and scorches the ground beneath its feet. Armed with searing weapons chained to their very forms, even a small band of fireborn can carve through enemy ranks without pause or fear, obeying every sadistic command of their cruel creators.

Yet for all the fel dwarves' devilish ingenuity, the demonic spirit animating these constructs is far from a stable power source. The imprisoned essence constantly seeks escape. When a fireborn suffers sufficient damage to its frame, the demon within begins tearing its way free, unraveling the construct from the inside. Rebellious flames burst through softened plates, erupting into the open as volcanic rock crumbles to the earth.

Despite this flaw, fireborn are usually able to win the day for their fel dwarf masters before collapsing. Their remains are then swiftly recovered, so that another wicked spirit may be shackled for the next campaign of conquest.


##### Infernal Fireborn Art Credit
* Flame-Kin Zealot - Arnie Swekel, Wizards of the Coast


\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

### Infernal Fireborn Tactics
Due to their Burning Bright trait, infernal fireborn function best as hard-hitting shock troopers—overwhelming enemies quickly before their power begins to wane. Their Blazing Body trait makes them most effective when targeting large groups of enemies.

##### Infernal Fireborn Adventure Hooks
| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Broken Frame:** A shattered infernal fireborn lies dormant in a battlefield-turned-graveyard, its armor split open and cold. Recently, scavengers who touched it have gone missing, and strange embers now rise from the wreckage each night. The party is hired to investigate—but the spirit within may not be as dormant as it seems.|
|  2  |**The Blazing Fugitive:** A single fireborn has broken free of its bindings and fled its masters. Now roaming the countryside in a mindless rage, it leaves trails of scorched earth and vaporized militia. The party is sent to destroy or subdue the rogue construct—but others seek to capture it and study how it resisted its creators.  |
|  3  | **The Chains That Burn:** A local noble has secretly acquired an Infernal Fireborn as a trophy. Bound by stolen rituals, it now guards his vault. But the binding is failing, and the party is hired to retrieve a relic locked inside—before the fireborn breaks loose and reduces the manor to molten ruin.|
|  4  |**The Ash March:** A column of fireborn is moving across the wastes without any visible escort or command. Scholars fear the daemonsmith who built them is dead—and that the constructs are now following their last order: to burn everything in their path. The party must find a way to stop or divert the march before it reaches a major settlement.  |

#### Optional: Describing Looted Materials
If you’re not interested in the specifics, simply say the party collected materials worth the rolled gp value. If you want more detail, the tables below suggest materials for different gp values by creature. They also provide **Example Names** and **Quality Descriptors** for items worth **half** or **twice** the table's gp value.

For example, a 10gp Metal item could be Fireborn Scrap, a 5gp version might be Worn Fireborn Scrap, and a 20gp version could be Masterwork Fireborn Scrap.

***When To Use Descriptions.*** You can describe these items during looting, when selling them, or when crafting, but it's best not to make players track long descriptive names. 

Only use as much detail as is needed when needed.

If you plan to use these creatures’ loot for crafting magic items, consult the Magic Themes table for thematic suggestions. Magic loot can span one or multiple themes.
 
For example, Fiendish magic item effects might drain the life of their victims or conjure unholy magic.

***Random Magic Ingredients.***
To introduce randomness to how often magic loot is found, roll a percentile die along with the normal loot roll to see if magic loot is found. There's a suggested probability at the top of the table.

***Magic Loot GP Values.*** The value of magic ingredients depends on your crafting system. Subtract their cost from the normal loot’s gp value. If the ingredient is worth significantly more, subtract it from the next treasure hoard instead.

> ### Traits
>
> ***Blazing Body.*** At the end of the fireborn’s turn, each other creature within 10 feet of it takes 7 (2d6) fire damage. 
>
> If the fireborn takes 5 or more cold damage, this trait doesn’t function at the end of the fireborn’s next turn.
>
> ***Burning Bright.*** At the start of the fireborn’s turn, if it has 140 or fewer hit points and took an action on its last turn, it gains a level of Instability and takes 20 force damage for each level of Instability it has. It removes a level of Instability at the end of any turn if it gained 20 or more hit points since its last turn.
>
> ***Fire Absorption.*** Whenever the fireborn is subjected to fire damage from a source other than itself, it takes no damage and instead regains a number of hit points equal to the fire damage dealt.
>
> ***Illumination.*** The fireborn sheds bright light in a 10-foot radius and dim light for an additional 10 feet.
>
> ***Immutable Form.*** The fireborn is immune to any spell or effect that would alter its form.

## Infernal Taurus
*Hellish Flying Bulls Formed From Elemental Fire*<br>
**Habitat:** Desert, Mountain, Planar (Elemental Plane <br> of Fire), Volcanic; **Treasure:** None <br>
When the winds of pyromantic magic gather and <br> consolidate in an area, destruction soon follows. Fires <br> sweep across the land, leaving only ash and ruin in their wake. The earth trembles, and volcanoes erupt from its tortured crust. Amid such magically wrought calamities, the coalescing powers of pyromancy may give birth to a creature that embodies pure, unrelenting destruction: the Infernal Taurus.

These hellish bovines are stubborn and wrathful, their anger quick to ignite. When provoked, their rage becomes terrifying to behold. As hatred begins to burn within the creature, its charred hide radiates with such heat that iron and steel melt upon contact. It paws the ground with obsidian hooves, sending white-hot sparks flying and branding the land with scorched gouges. Tendrils of dark smoke pour from its flaring nostrils, and its eyes blaze like twin torches. With a beat of massive crimson wings, it streaks through the air like a blazing comet, its brimstone horns skewering and searing all in its path.

Fortunately, these fearsome incarnations wither and crumble to ash within days if deprived of the intense magical heat that birthed them. Thus, they can only endure in places of great fire—scorching deserts, volcanic wastes, or the Plane of Fire itself.

Yet the fel dwarves venerate these beasts for their rage, resilience, and capacity for wanton destruction. Their daemonsmiths construct vast ritual furnaces to sustain the infernal taurus, keeping them compliant and ready to be unleashed upon lush lands ripe for immolation.


Maintaining such brutal power is perilous. The fires that sustain a taurus must be constantly fed with incantations and blood sacrifices. Should the flame falter, the beast's wrath turns upon its keepers. Only the most ambitious and foolhardy warlords dare to make these monsters their mounts, nailing saddles of enchanted brass into their flesh to survive the heat. Such lords are spoken of with dread—for when one of these tyrants rises into the sky upon a blazing bull above the battlefield like a blazing sun, it is a harbinger of doom.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>


### Baleful Taurus

At the greatest confluence of pyromantic energies, an even more terrible creature is born—the Baleful Taurus. These monsters eclipse even the infernal taurus in their capacity to unleash burning calamity. With its sinewed limbs, it stamps the earth, sending waves of molten rock rippling outward. A single beat of its flame-wreathed wings summons gales of scorching ash that flay skin and blind the unprepared.

The most powerful overseers and daemonsmiths pay dearly in wealth and blood to bind such an embodiment of fire to their will.

### Infernal Taurus Tactics
Infernal taurus are most effective when charging between targets to maximize the use of their Gore and Stomp attacks. They are able to dive bomb targets this way from the sky as an opening move, choosing targets that rely on melee weapons as their preferred targets. Their Resolute feature provides significant benefits, so they will attempt to maintain it whenever possible—even if doing so means attacking suboptimal targets. 

#### Baleful Taurus Tactics
Baleful Taurus are more flexible in combat, able to forgo standard attacks in favor of the following abilities:

**Molten Smash.** This ability is always used if the Taurus can hit three or more targets, or if it failed to knock a creature prone this turn.

**Cinder Gale.** This is favored when there are no optimal targets to charge or if the Taurus is unable to move.

style='position:absolute;top:-160px;left:-0px;width:860px;transform: scaleX(1)' />

##### Infernal Taurus Adventure Hooks
| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Tyrant's Mount:** A fel dwarf champion is preparing for conquest astride an infernal taurus, but the saddle-ritual is incomplete. The party is hired to infiltrate the forges before the final binding is complete, to sabotage the process—or slay the beast before it becomes unstoppable.|
|  2  | **The Dying Furnace:** A ritual furnace that sustains an infernal taurus deep beneath a fel dwarf keep is beginning to fail. The beast grows more unstable by the hour, and the fortress risks complete incineration if it breaks free. A rebel faction within the keep hires the party to hasten the collapse as part of a wider revolt.  |
|  3  | **The Burning Tomb:** A forgotten tomb, once sealed with molten stone, now vents smoke and fire. An infernal taurus, imprisoned centuries ago by an ancient pyromancer order, has begun to stir. The party must discover the reason for its return—and determine if the creature is being awakened or escaping.|
|  4  |**The Baleful Bounty:** A powerful daemonsmith has promised a vast reward to any who help him trap a newly-manifested baleful taurus to serve as his personal siege mount. The party may be hired to assist—or recruited by a rival faction to ensure the beast is never controlled by anyone. |

> ## Infernal Taurus
> *Large elemental (mini-boss), lawful evil*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 17      **Initiative** +5 (15)
> - **Hit Points** 200 (16d12 + 96)
> - **Speed** 50 ft., fly 50 ft.

> - **Skills** Intimidation +7, Perception +6
> - **Damage Immunities** Fire
> - **Damage Resistances** Cold, Poison
> - **Senses** Darkvision 120 ft., Passive Perception 16
> - **Languages** understands Infernal and Primordial (Ignan) but can’t speak
> - **Challenge** 12 (8,400 XP)      **Proficiency Bonus** +4

> ### Traits
> ***Burning Resolve.*** When the taurus becomes Resolute*, it and each creature within 10 feet of it start Burning*, taking 10 (4d4) fire damage at the end of each of their turns until the condition ends.
>
> ***Fire Absorption.*** Whenever the taurus is subjected to fire damage from a source other than itself, it takes no damage and instead regains a number of hit points equal to the fire damage dealt.
>
> ***Molten Resolve.*** Whenever a nonmagical weapon hits the taurus while it is Resolute*, the object takes a -1 penalty to attack rolls. It is destroyed if the penalty reaches -5.
>
> ### Actions
> ***Multiattack.*** The taurus makes one Gore attack and one Pulverizing Stomp attack.
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +11 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 20 (2d12 + 7) piercing damage plus 11 (2d10) fire damage. If the taurus moved at least 20 feet straight toward the target immediately before the hit, the target must succeed on a *Strength Saving Throw:* DC 19. <bR>
> *Failure:* The target is knocked prone and pushed up to 20 feet away.
>
> ***Pulverizing Stomp.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +11 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 20 (2d12 + 7) bludgeoning damage plus 11 (2d10) fire damage. If the target is prone, it takes an additional 11 (2d10) fire damage and can’t stand until the end of its next turn unless it spends all its movement to make a Constitution saving throw. On a success, it stands up.
>
> ### Bonus Actions
>
> ***Resolute Charge.*** At the start of its turn, the taurus may move up to its speed in a straight line and become Resolute*.
>

\pagebreakNum

> ##### New Condition: Resolute
> The creature stubbornly digs in to weather any assault. It experiences the following effects:
> * Attack rolls made against the creature have disadvantage.
> * The creature can't take its move action on its turn.
> * The creature makes Strength checks and all saving throws with advantage, except Dexterity saving throws, which it makes with disadvantage.
The Resolute condition ends if an effect moves the creature against its will, knocks it prone, or the creature becomes charmed, frightened, or incapacitated. A creature that is prone, charmed, frightened, or incapacitated can't become Resolute.

> ### Traits
>
> ***Burning Resolve.*** When the taurus becomes Resolute*, it and each creature within 10 feet of it start Burning*, taking 12 (5d4) fire damage at the start of each of their turns until the condition ends.
>
> ***Fire Absorption.*** Whenever the taurus is subjected to fire damage from a source other than itself, it takes no damage and instead regains a number of hit points equal to the fire damage dealt.
>
> ***Molten Resolve.*** Whenever a nonmagical weapon hits the taurus while it is Resolute*, the object takes a -1 penalty to attack rolls. It is destroyed if the penalty reaches -5.

> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The taurus makes one Gore attack and one Pulverizing Stomp attack. If the taurus is Resolute*, it can either replace its Gore with a Cinder Gale or its Pulverizing Stomp with a Molten Smash.
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +13 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 27 (3d12 + 8) piercing damage plus 16 (3d10) fire damage. If the taurus moved at least 20 feet straight toward the target immediately before the hit, the target must succeed on a *Strength Saving Throw:* DC 20. <br>
> *Failure:* The target is knocked Prone and pushed up to 20 feet away.
>
> ***Pulverizing Stomp.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +13 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 27 (3d12 + 8) bludgeoning damage plus 16 (3d10) fire damage. If the target is Prone, it takes an additional 11 (2d10) fire damage and can’t stand until the end of its next turn unless it spends all its movement to make a DC 19 Constitution saving throw. On a success, it stands up.
>
> ***Cinder Gale (3/Day).*** Each creature in a 20-foot-wide, 60-foot-long line must make a *Constitution Saving Throw:* DC 21. <br>
> *Failure:* 21 (6d6) fire damage, and the target is pushed 15 feet away from the taurus. <br>
> *Failure by 5+:* The target is Blinded until the end of the taurus’s next turn. <br>
> *Success:* Half damage only.
>
> ***Molten Smash (3/Day).*** Each creature in a 15-foot emanating from the taurus must make a Dexterity or Strength saving throw: DC 21. <br>
> *Failure:* 10 (3d6) fire damage plus 10 (3d6) bludgenoing damage, and the target is knocked prone. <br>
> *Failure by 5+:* The target can’t stand until the end of its next turn unless it spends all its movement to make a DC 20 Constitution saving throw. On a success, it stands up. <br>
> *Success:* Half damage only. <br>
> *Success or Failure:* The ground in the area becomes difficult terrain if it is made of earth or stone.
>

> ***Resolute Charge.*** At the start of its turn, the taurus may move up to its speed in a straight line and become Resolute*.

\pagebreakNum

> ##### New Condition: Burning
> The creature has been set ablaze by something that continues to damage it each round until it is extinguished. The default source described here is fire, but other sources could deal different types of damage, such as acid. 
> * **Default Damage:** A burning creature takes 1d4 fire damage at the end of each of its turns unless the source that inflicted the condition states otherwise.
> * **Ending the Condition:** As an action, the burning creature can extinguish the fire by dropping prone and rolling on the ground. The fire also goes out if it is doused, submerged, or suffocated. For example, another creature could use an action to put out the flames with their cloak or by pouring water on them.
> * **Multiple Sources of Burning:** If a burning creature would gain this condition again from another source, the new burning effect only replaces the old if it deals more damage each round. Otherwise, it is ignored.

<bR>

### Infernal Taurus Loot
Valuable infernal taurus loot typically comes from harvested materials and usually requires a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Arcana)** check. You may also allow players proficient in specific tools to harvest relevant items (e.g., a **Wisdom (Leatherworker’s Tools)** check to gather Hide). 

Alternatively, you can roll for loot randomly using a flat modifier.

##### Infernal Taurus Loot (Avg. 550gp)

| Looting Check Result <br> or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-9  | 2d4(5) 50gp Items (250gp) |
|  10-13 | 1d6(3) 100gp Items (300gp) | 
|  14-20 | 2d4(5) 100gp Items (500gp) |  
|  21-25 | 1d6(3) 200gp Items (600gp)  |  
|  26+ |  2d6(7) 200gp Items (1,400gp) |  

##### Baleful Taurus Loot (Avg. 1,775gp)

| Looting Check Result <br> or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-10  | 1 500gp Items (500gp) |
|  11-14 | 1 1,000gp Items (1,000gp) | 
|  15-21 | 1d4(2) 1,000gp Items (2,000gp) |  
|  22-25 | 1 2,000gp Items (2,000gp)  |  
|  26+ |  1d4(2) 2,000gp Items (4,000gp) |  

\columnbreak 

#### Optional: Describing Looted Materials
If you’re not interested in the specifics, simply say the party collected materials worth the rolled gp value. If you want more detail, the tables below suggest materials for different gp values by creature. They also provide **Example Names** and **Quality Descriptors** for items worth **half** or **twice** the table's gp value.

For example, a 100gp Bone item from an infernal taurus could be a Taurus Horn, a 50gp version might be a Cracked Taurus Horn, and a 200gp version could be a Pristine Taurus Horn.

***When To Use Descriptions.*** You can describe these items during looting, when selling them, or when crafting, but it's best not to make players track long descriptive names. Only use as much detail as is needed when needed.



##### Infernal Taurus Materials: 100gp 

|1d4 | Material | Example Name (Quality Descriptors) | 
|:--:|:---:|:-----------:|
| 1   | Bone|   Taurus Horn (Cracked/Pristine) | 
| 2   | Flesh | Taurus Heart (Damaged/Pristine)|  
| 3   | Fluid|  Taurus Blood (Clotted/Thick) |  
| 4  | Hide |Taurus Hide (Tattered/Tough) | 
 

 

##### Baleful Taurus Materials: 1,000gp 

|1d4 | Material | Example Name (Quality Descriptors) | 
|:--:|:---:|:-----------:|
| 1   | Bone|  Baleful Taurus Fang (Cracked/Pristine) | 
| 2   | Flesh | Baleful Taurus Heart (Damaged/Pristine)|  
| 3   | Fluid| Baleful Taurus Blood (Clotted/Thick) |  
| 4  | Hide | Baleful Taurus Skin (Tattered/Tough) |  

#### Optional: Magic Loot for Item Crafting
If you plan to use harvested loot for crafting magic items, you can try to thematically align the effects of the magic items being crafted with the creature's they're harvested from. In the case of infernal taurus, Fire effects would make the most sense. These could be magic item effects that create light, conjure fire spells, or embolden allies.

***Magic Loot GP Values.*** The value of magic ingredients depends on your crafting system. Subtract their cost from the normal loot’s gp value. If the ingredient is worth significantly more, subtract it from the next treasure hoard instead.

## Zhartahn, The Dark
*Dwarven Tyrant of Cruel Domination*<br>
**Habitat:** Desert, Mountain, Underdark, Urban, Volcanic; **Treasure:** Armaments <br>

In the ash-choked badlands, where once green things grew and flourished and now only the wicked thrive, there rise into the sky a monolith of black whose shadows fall long even through the ashen winds that veil the cursed land in a sorrowful haze. 

If one were to brave those bleak and lifeless wastes, they would come upon a city torn from the dreams of demons and hammered into being by hate—where factories scream horrid songs and foul smoke billows from their roofs, as twisted engines of death are birthed. Great temples of tarnished bronze stand as an affront to all that is sacred, their walls adorned with carved effigies of horned and hideous gods—bovine lords hewn in obsidian, before whom blasphemous rites are offered. And ever above them all rise towers wrought of blackest iron, spearing the smothered sky, where the demon-smiths hold counsel and overlook with pride the hellscape they have wrought.

Yet not in those dread halls are the vilest works performed, but rather far below, in the bowels of the earth itself. There, beneath the streets and furnaces, are the true horrors made manifest. The slave-pits stretch deep into the bones of the world to gather its poisonous wealth, and within them, throngs of broken souls labour without rest, goaded on by cruel taskmasters. And among these, none are more feared than Zhartahn the Dark.

Zhartahn, who hungers for agony, is the most beloved of the priest-smiths, for his cruelty yields vast tribute.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

 When his thralls falter, Zhartahn devises fresh torments, crafting pain with as much care as an artist might hew a statue from marble. Thus, the mines flourish beneath his ire, though the life is soon drained from all who toil within.


And when the mines are emptied of strength and the pits echo only with death, Zhartahn rises again with his host of fel warriors, clad in infernal mail and bearing weapons born of hatred and hell. Beyond the blasted lands they march, into the green and living world, that he might bring back new souls to feed the city’s ever-hungering forges. The folk of the fields are taken in chains.
So great is the malice of his tongue, and so heavy the dread in his voice, that even armed hosts falter. Steel stays, and hearts crumble. Many cast down their blades and kneel, pleading for mercy—yet Zhartahn has none to give. Their submission only stokes the fire of his wicked joy.

But those few who resist—who dare to rise against his coming—earn only his wrath. With obsidian axes he carves ruin into their ranks, each stroke a harbinger of pain, each wound a vessel of torment. Even the bravest fall shrieking, their courage undone.
So has it always been. No city, no fortress, no army has yet broken the yoke of Zhartahn. All are brought to heel, and their people bound in service to the black city and the demon-smiths who rule it.

Yet in the shadows of that dread dominion, among the tattered remnants of conquered peoples, there flickers still a spark. Some yet believe that Zhartahn shall one day be met not with fear, but with defiance—that a company of souls, unbent and unbroken, shall rise to end his boundless cruelty.

<img
src='https://i.postimg.cc/XYC85pVV/Balthorthe-Defiledcopy2-5000x.webp'
style='position:absolute;top:-158px;left:-0px;width:870px;transform: scaleX(1)' />

### Zhartahn & Abarzug's Lair

Zhartahn and Abarzug make their lairs in a fel dwarf garrison tower amid a grand city. Below are miles of volcanic tunnels where all manner of slaves toil under the cruel supervision of armed fel dwarves to harvest valuable minerals. These slaves will fight to the death if commanded to do so, for to die in battle would be a sweet release compared to the punishment that would follow if they refuse the commands of their dark masters.

When fighting within their lair, Zhartahn and Abarzug's Challenge Ratings (CR) increase by 1.

#### Lair Action
When either Zhartahn or Abarzug rolls initiative, their lair awakens to aid them. Until combat ends or both die, the lair has an Intelligence of 16 and can act of its own accord, always acting in the best interest of both. While active in this way, the lair is aware of the location of all creatures within it. On initiative count 0 (losing initiative ties), the lair chooses two Subjugated Workers within it (stat block found after Zhartahn and Abarzug's). They gain 20 temporary hit points for the next minute. While they have these temporary hit points, they are dominated (as described in their stat block) and under the control of the lair.

Whenever a dominated target receives an effect that would end the Frightened or Charmed condition, it loses all of its temporary hit points and ceases to be dominated.

\columnbreak

#### Regional Effects
The area where Zhartahn and Abarzug dwell is corrupted by their presence, creating one or more of the following effects everywhere within 5 miles of their lair:

* Whenever a creature hostile to Zhartahn or Abarzug is reduced to 0 hit points within the area, it must make a *Charisma Saving Throw:* DC 18.<br>
*Failure:* For the next hour, it cannot cause creatures to be Charmed or Frightened by it, and the creature has disadvantage on Charisma checks and saving throws against being Charmed or Frightened.
* Whenever a creature hostile to Zhartahn or Abarzug attempts to telepathically communicate in the area, it must make an *Intelligence Saving Throw:* DC 18.<br>
*Failure:* It takes 18 (4d8) psychic damage and fails to communicate.<br>
*Success:* It can communicate telepathically for the next 10 minutes without having to make a saving throw.
* Water sources within 5 miles of the lair are supernaturally warm and tainted with sulfur.
* Storms of hot ash are frequent.



### Epic Battle: Twin Lords of Suffering
If you want to have Zhartahn and Abarzug work together to make a true endgame threat, make the following changes to them and treat them as having a combined Challenge Rating (CR) or 23:

* Whenever Zhartahn or Abarzug gain Cruelty, the other also gains the same amount of Cruelty.
* Whenever Zhartahn or Abarzug dies the other gains five levels of Cruelty

>
> ***Obsidian Axe.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +9 to hit (with advantage if it is an attack of opportunity), reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 13 (2d8 + 4) Slashing damage plus Psychic damage equal to amount Cruelty he has. Zhartahn then gains one level of Cruelty if the target is Frightened or Restrained. If the target is reduced to 0 hit points, it is Stunned for 1 minute, and Zhartahn gains three levels of Cruelty.
>
>
> ***Blunderbuss.*** *Ranged Weapon Attack:* +9 to hit (ignores half and three-quarters cover, and disadvantage from long range while Zhartahn is Resolute*), range 80/320 ft., one target. *Hit:* 26 (4d10 + 4) Piercing damage plus Psychic damage equal to amount Cruelty he has, and the target’s speed is reduced by 10 ft. until the end of its next turn. Zhartahn can’t make this attack again until he reloads the weapon as an action or becomes Resolute*.
>
> ***Sadistic Snare (3/Day).*** *Dexterity Saving Throw:* DC 17, One Large or smaller target Zhartahn can see within 30 feet <br>
> *Failure:* The target is Restrained until the snare is destroyed (AC 18; HP 15; immunity to Bludgeoning, Poison, and Psychic damage). A creature can take an action to make a DC 17 Strength (Athletics) check to free itself or another creature in a net within 5 feet, destroying the net on a success. If a creature ends its turn in the net, Zhartahn gains one level of Cruelty.
>
> ### Bonus Actions
>
> ***Resolute Stance.*** At the start of Zhartahn’s turn, he becomes Resolute* until the start of his next turn.
>
> ### Monstrous Actions
>
> Zhartahn gains two additional actions in combat: Subjugating Order and Tyrant’s Claim. Each action can be performed on its own initiative count, separate from Zhartahn's. On the action's initiative count (losing ties), Zhartahn can take the action if he is not Incapacitated. He can replace either action with Tenacious Will, even if Incapacitated.
>
> ***Subjugating Order (Initiative Count 21).*** *Wisdom Saving Throw:* DC 18, two creatures within 60 feet of Zhartahn that were not targeted by this ability during the last round <br>
> *Failure:* The target becomes Frightened of Zhartahn, and Zhartahn gains one level of Cruelty. While Frightened in this way, the target is also Charmed by Zhartahn. The Frightened target can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself on a success. If it fails this saving throw, it falls Prone, and Zhartahn gains one level of Cruelty.
>
> ***Tyrant’s Claim (Initiative Count 1).*** Zhartahn lets loose a claim of his dominance. Any creature within 25 feet of Zhartahn that is not Frightened or Restrained can challenge him. If more than one creature challenges him, he can choose one. Zhartahn or a creature he is mounted on can then move up to 25 feet towards a chosen creature that challenged him, and then Zhartahn makes an attack against that creature, dealing an additional 13 (3d8) slashing damage on hit. If no creature challenges Zhartahn, he gains five levels of Cruelty.
>
>
> ***Tenacious Will.*** If Zhartahn is subject to an ongoing effect that allows him to make a saving throw as an action or at the start or end of his turn, he can immediately make that save with advantage, ending the effect on a success.
>

</span>

> ### Traits
>
> ***Boundless Cruelty.*** At the start of each of Abarzug’s turns during combat, he gains one level of Cruelty. He loses all levels of Cruelty when combat ends.
>
> ***Magic Resistance.*** Abarzug has advantage on saving throws against spells and other magical effects.
>
> ***Sorcerous Miasma.*** Abarzug emits a miasma in a 10-foot radius emanating from himself. The properties and powers of magic items are suppressed while within the miasma. For example, a +1 longsword in the miasma functions as a nonmagical longsword. A magic weapon’s properties and powers are suppressed if it is used against a target in the miasma or wielded by an attacker in the miasma. If a magic weapon or piece of magic ammunition leaves the miasma (e.g., a magic arrow fired at a target outside the miasma), its magic properties cease to be suppressed as soon as it exits.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** Abarzug makes two attacks: one with his Bite and one with his Claws. If both attacks hit the same target, the target is Grappled (escape DC 17). Until this Grapple ends, Abarzug cannot use his Bite or Claws against another target.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +9 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 14 (2d8 + 5) Piercing damage plus Psychic damage equal to the number of Cruelty levels Abarzug has. If the target is Prone, the attack deals 23 (4d8 + 5) Piercing damage plus Psychic damage equal to twice the number of Cruelty levels Abarzug has, and Abarzug then gains three levels of Cruelty.
>
> ***Claws.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +9 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 10 (1d10 + 5) Slashing damage plus Psychic damage equal to the number of Cruelty levels Abarzug has. If Abarzug moved at least 10 feet straight toward the target immediately before the hit, the target must succeed on a DC 17 Strength saving throw or be knocked Prone.
>
> ### Monstrous Actions
>
> Abarzug gains two additional actions in combat: Ghastly Prison and Withering Breath. Each action can be performed on its own initiative count, separate from Abarzug's. On the action's initiative count (losing ties), Abarzug can take the action if he is not Incapacitated. He can replace either action with Tenacious Will, even if Incapacitated.
>
> ***Ghastly Prison (Initiative Count 23).*** *Intelligence Saving Throw:* DC 18, two creatures within 60 feet of Abarzug that were not targeted by this ability during the last round <br>
> *Failure:* Abarzug gains one level of Cruelty, and the target becomes sheathed in phantasms. While sheathed in phantasms, the creature is unable to see anything farther than 10 feet away and Abarzug gains one level of Cruelty at the end of each of the creature’s turns. If the creature willingly moves 5 feet or more, it takes 18 (4d8) Psychic damage, and the effect ends. The target can use its action to examine the phantasm by making a DC 18 Intelligence (Investigation) check; if the check succeeds, the target realizes the phantasm is an illusion, and the effect ends.
>
> ***Withering Breath (On Initiative Count 3).*** Abarzug may move up to 25 feet and then force each creature in a 30-foot cone to make a *Wisdom Saving Throw:* DC 17.<br>
> *Failure:* Abarzug gains one level of Cruelty, and the creature’s mind becomes filled with doubt until initiative count 1 of the next round. While filled with doubt, the target has disadvantage on all ability checks and saving throws, and attack rolls against it have advantage.
> 
> ***Tenacious Will.*** If Abarzug is subject to an ongoing effect that allows him to make a saving throw as an action or at the start or end of his turn, he can immediately make that save with advantage, ending the effect on a success.

</span>


### Zhartahn's Tactics
Zhartahn wins through attrition—growing stronger as the battle drags on and accumulating Cruelty until he can crush his foes.

**Subjugating Order.** Zhartahn targets two creatures with the lowest Wisdom saving throws or highest remaining hit points, aiming to incapacitate and remove them from the fight early.

**Normal Turn Sequence.** Zhartahn begins by using Resolute Stance to prolong his presence on the battlefield and build Cruelty. He then snares the nearest target and follows up with an Obsidian Axe attack. If no enemies are in melee range, he snares a target with low Dexterity and shoots them with his Blunderbuss.

**Tyrant’s Claim.** This ability is reactive and dependent on enemy behavior. Zhartahn can use it to reduce the number of enemies that can challenge him by inflicting Frightened or Restrained conditions, ideally disabling as many opponents as possible.

\columnbreak

### Abarzug's Tactics
Abarzug also fights a war of attrition, using flight to avoid being surrounded and control positioning.

**Ghastly Prison.** Abarzug targets two closely grouped enemies, prioritizing those with low Intelligence saving throws. This limits their ability to spread out and makes them more vulnerable to his Withering Breath.

**Normal Turn Sequence.** Abarzug targets a creature with low Strength, under the effects of Withering Breath, or one that is isolated, and tries to  Grapple it and drag it into a more favorable position.

**Withering Breath.** Abarzug uses this as soon as he can affect multiple enemies. Ideally, his Ghastly Prison and movement on prior turns have maneuvered targets into a tightly packed group for maximum effect.
 
### Subjugated Worker Tactics
The primary goal of the subjugated workers is to help accumulate Cruelty. They attack any targets they can gain advantage against and are considered expendable—often positioned to be struck by Withering Breath to further fuel cruelty gain.

##### Zhartahn, The Dark Adventure Hooks
| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The March of Iron and Smoke:** Zhartahn the Dark has launched a brutal campaign across the borderlands, leading his forces atop Abarzug, whose psychic influence leaves entire garrisons paralyzed with fear before the battle begins. The party is hired by a desperate alliance of frontier lords to assassinate Zhartahn—or find a way to sever the bond between him and the lammasu|
|  2  | **The Burnt Standard:** Zhartahn has defiled a sacred dwarven monument, melting its ancestral runes into slag to forge a new standard for his legion. Now, the spirits of the fallen clans cry for vengeance. The party is enlisted to recover the desecrated relic from the heart of Zhartahn’s war camp |
|  3  | **Chains for the Sun:** Zhartahn has enslaved a fire elemental shrine and forced it to burn perpetually to fuel his forges. Abarzug has taken up residence near the altar, warping the local ley lines with his presence. The area suffers from unnatural eclipses and solar flares. The party is approached by sun priests or elemental guardians who need help purging the shrine and breaking Zhartahn’s hold.|
|  4  |**The Black Procession:** Zhartahn is escorting a caravan of chained prisoners and infernal war machines toward a gate said to lead into the Plane of Fire. He intends to trade the captives—and a secret artifact—to a fiery lord in exchange for a legion of flameborn horrors. The party must intercept the procession before the pact is sealed, or venture into the Plane of Fire to undo it after the fact. |

\pagebreakNum




### Zhartahn's Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from fel dwarves are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying or hiding nearby. Most dropped or hidden valuables can be found using **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Wisdom (Perception)** checks. 

Valuable lammasu loot typically comes from harvested materials and usually requires a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Arcana)** check. You may also allow players proficient in specific tools to harvest relevant items (e.g., a **Wisdom (Leatherworker’s Tools)** check to gather Hide). 

Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.


##### Zhartahn, The Dark & Abarzug, the Tormenter Loot Table  (Avg. 1,500gp)

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-9  | 1 500gp Item |
|  10-13 | 1d4(2) 500gp Items | 
|  14-20 | 1 1,000gp Item  |  
|  21-25 | 1 2,000gp Item |  
|  26+ |  1d4(2) 2,000gp Items |  



### Optional: Describing Looted Materials
If you’re not interested in the specifics, simply say the party collected materials worth the rolled gp value. If you want more detail, the tables below suggest materials for different gp values by creature. They also provide **Example Names** and **Quality Descriptors** for items worth **half** or **twice** the table's gp value.



For example, a 1,000gp Bone item from a Zhartahn could be a Tyrant's Trophy Skull, a 500gp version might be a Cracked Tyrant's Trophy Skull, and a 2,000gp version could be a Pristine Tyrant's Trophy Skull.

***When To Use Descriptions.*** You can describe these items during looting, when selling them, or when crafting, but it's best not to make players track long descriptive names. Only use as much detail as is needed when needed.

#### Optional: Magic Loot for Item Crafting
If you plan to use harvested loot for crafting magic items, you can try to thematically align the effects of the magic items being crafted with the creature's they're harvested from. In the case of Zhartahn and Abarzug, Fiendish effects would make the most sense. These could be magic item effects that steal the lives of their victims or conjure unholy magic.

***Magic Loot GP Values.*** The value of magic ingredients depends on your crafting system. Subtract their cost from the normal loot’s gp value. If the ingredient is worth significantly more, subtract it from the next treasure hoard instead.


<br>
 
> ##### New Condition: Resolute
> The creature stubbornly digs in to weather any assault. It experiences the following effects:
> * Attack rolls made against the creature have disadvantage.
> * The creature can't take its move action on its turn.
> * The creature makes Strength checks and all saving throws with advantage, except Dexterity saving throws, which it makes with disadvantage.
The Resolute condition ends if an effect moves the creature against its will, knocks it prone, or the creature becomes charmed, frightened, or incapacitated. A creature that is prone, charmed, frightened, or incapacitated can't become Resolute.

<br>

* Brass's Tunnel-Grinder - Cristi Balanescu, Wizards of the Coast

# Self-Propelled Vehicles
Most land vehicles in fantasy settings are pulled by other creatures, such as wagons, carriages, or chariots. However, through some combination of technology or magic, some vehicles may be self-propelled and driven by a passenger. These may be relatively small mechanical contraptions, magically self-propelled carriages, or mighty war machines rumbling across blasted battlefields. 

The following rules can help you codify how to use these vehicle types in your games. They can be applied to vehicles of different shapes and sizes and used as tools for designing your own vehicles. The rules here can be applied to most self-powered vehicles piloted by a passenger. 

## Self-Propelled Vehicle Rules
Self-propelled vehicles are vehicles able to move without needing to be pushed or pulled by another creature, and they usually don’t need an external energy source (such as wind). Throughout this document, they will be referred to simply as vehicles. Creatures within a vehicle are referred to as passengers. 
In combat, vehicles use most of the same rules as creatures, with the following additional considerations:

### Opportunity Attacks
Vehicles provoke opportunity attacks as usual. When a vehicle provokes an opportunity attack, the attacker can target the vehicle itself or any creature riding on or inside it, provided they are within reach and do not have total cover.



\columnbreak

### Spacing Within Vehicles
All creatures within a vehicle count as being within 5 feet of each other.


### Entering and Exiting Vehicles
Entering or exiting the vehicle costs a creature half of its movement. Each creature inside the vehicle may use its reaction to make an opportunity attack against the creature entering or exiting.


### Crashing into Creatures and Objects
A vehicle can crash into a creature or object by entering its space. When it does, the creature or object must make a Dexterity or Strength saving throw (the target's choice) using the vehicle's DC. On a failed save, the target takes 1d6 bludgeoning damage for every 10 feet the vehicle moved in a straight line before attempting to enter the target's space (maximum 20d6 damage).

If the target is a creature, it is also knocked prone. On a successful Dexterity save, the target takes no damage and is not knocked prone. On a successful Strength save, the creature takes half damage, is not knocked prone, and the vehicle's speed becomes 0 until the end of the turn. A target can only make this saving throw once per turn.

If the vehicle is at least two size categories larger than the target it crashed into, it can continue moving through the target's space if it has any movement remaining. Otherwise, the vehicle comes to a sudden stop. If the target is an impassable object that could reasonably damage the vehicle, such as an iron wall, the vehicle comes to a sudden stop and takes 1d6 bludgeoning damage for every 10 feet it moved since its last turn (maximum 20d6 damage). Each creature on or inside the vehicle takes the damage as well

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/7VQV8VK/ballista-charger.png' style='position:absolute; top:-0px; right:0px; width:817px; transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:45px; right:100px; width:950px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(4deg)' />


<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:100px; right:-200px; width:900px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(0deg)' />

\pagebreakNum

### Prone Vehicles
If vehicle falls prone, it cannot right itself and is incapacitated until it is flipped upright.

### Falling Vehicles
When a vehicle falls from a height of 10 feet or higher, it and all creatures on or inside it take damage from the fall as normal and land in a prone position. If the vehicle falls due to the actions of its driver (such as jumping off a ramp) it may not land prone (DM’s discretion) but still takes fall damage.



### Repairing Vehicles
If a vehicle has taken damage but still has at least 1 hit point, a creature can spend 1 hour or more attempting to repair the damage. The vehicle must be stationary, and the creature must have the necessary tools and parts for the repairs. After 1 hour of repair work, the creature makes an Intelligence check, adding its proficiency bonus to the check if it is proficient with the tools required for the repairs. If the check succeeds, the vehicle regains 2d4 + its Intelligence modifier + its proficiency bonus hit points. If the check fails, the vehicle does not regain any hit points, but the repair can be attempted again using the same tools and replacement parts.

### Vehicular Exhaustion 
Certain circumstances can cause a vehicle to malfunction and eventually break down due to wear and tear. This wear and tear can be represented using exhaustion rules, as described in Appendix A of the Player's Handbook, with the following modifications:

* When a vehicle reaches exhaustion level 6, its hit points drop to 0, and the vehicle breaks down.
* The only way to remove the effects of exhaustion on a vehicle is through repair. This can be done using the <br> rules described in the Repairing Vehicles section <br> above. If the attempt to repair the vehicle <br> succeeds, the vehicle's exhaustion level <br> decreases by 1. If the check fails, the <br> vehicle's exhaustion level remains <br> unchanged, but the repair attempt <br> can be made again using <br> the same tools and <br> replacement parts.

\columnbreak

## Self-Propelled Vehicle Attributes
Besides the size, weight, AC, HP, and damage immunity attributes common to all objects, these vehicles have the following additional attributes and considerations:

### Hit Points 
A vehicle's hit points can be restored through vehicle repairs. However, when a vehicle's hit points reach 0, it becomes inoperative and is irreparably damaged.
### Damage Threshold
Most vehicles possess bulk or armor that enables them to withstand minor hits. A vehicle with a damage threshold is immune to all damage unless the amount of damage it takes is equal to or greater than its damage threshold value. In such cases, the vehicle takes damage as usual. Damage that fails to meet or exceed the vehicle's damage threshold is considered superficial and does not reduce the vehicle's hit points.

### Mishap Threshold
When a vehicle sustains damage from a single source that is equal to or exceeds its mishap threshold, it is required to roll on the Mishaps table (refer to the Mishaps section).

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/pZzQTPR/surgehacker-mech.png' style='position:absolute; bottom:-100px; right:-200px; width:1016px; transform:scaleX(-1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-410px; right:-170px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(0deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-300px; right:105px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(-37deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-451px; right:-00px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(-4deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

\pagebreakNum

### Creature Capacity 
Creature capacity determines the number of creatures that can ride the vehicle comfortably. Additional creatures can fit by squeezing or clinging to the outside of the vehicle.

### Cargo Capacity
Cargo capacity indicates the maximum weight of cargo the vehicle can carry.

### Vehicle DC 
Whenever the vehicle requires a creature to make a check or saving throw, it uses this number as the DC.

### Challenge Rating
When players face enemies that are equipped with a fully functioning vehicle, the challenge rating (CR) of the encounter should be calculated as if the vehicle is an additional creature with its own CR.

### Ability Scores 
A vehicle possesses the standard six ability scores that creatures have, along with their corresponding modifiers. The Strength of the vehicle is determined by its size and weight, while Dexterity represents its handling and maneuverability. The Constitution of a vehicle reflects its durability and quality of construction. In most cases, vehicles have a score of 0 in Intelligence, Wisdom, and Charisma.

If a vehicle has a score of 0 in a particular ability score, it automatically fails any ability check or saving throw that relies on that score.

### Action Stations
A vehicle may have one or more Action Stations. Each of these stations requires a certain number of creatures to operate and may grant those creatures some amount of cover. The creatures operating these stations must be passengers within the vehicle, but not all passengers need to be operating a station. A creature operating a station <br> can use an action to activate the station's effect.  <br> A station can be occupied by only one <br> creature at a time and can only <br> be activated once per round. 

\columnbreak

#### The Helm 
Most vehicles that must be piloted by a passenger (referred to as the driver) have an Action Station known as the Helm, where the vehicle's movement is controlled. It usually consists of a chair equipped with a wheel, levers, pedals, and other controls. If a vehicle has a helm with no one operating it, it automatically fails Dexterity saving throws. A driver who is proficient with land vehicles can add their proficiency bonus to ability checks and saving throws made using the vehicle's ability scores.

The driver can use an action to propel the vehicle up to its speed or bring it to a complete stop. While the vehicle is in motion, the driver can steer it along any desired course. If the driver becomes incapacitated, leaves the helm, or takes no action to alter the vehicle's course and speed, the vehicle will continue moving in the same direction and at the same speed as it did during the driver's last turn until it collides with an obstacle large enough to stop its movement.


### Mishaps
Most vehicles have a Mishaps Table, which describes different ways its functionality can go awry under adverse conditions. When certain abilities or conditions dictate, roll on this Mishaps Table. 

To resolve a Mishap, a creature can use its action to make an ability check based on the nature of the mishap (refer to the Mishaps section). If the vehicle is moving, the check is made with disadvantage. If the creature is proficient with the tools required for the repairs and has them at hand, it adds its proficiency bonus to the check. A successful check ends the mishap. Mishaps that do not have a Repair Check Type cannot be repaired.

##### Self-Propelled Vehicles Art Credit
* Ballista Charger - Sung Choi, Wizards of the Coast
* Surgehacker Mech - Wisnu Tan, Wizards of the Coast
* Dermotaxi - Mark Zug, Wizards of the Coast

\pagebreakNum

#  Siege Weapons
These weapons have been engineered for large-scale warfare against enemy armies and settlements. What sets them apart from other weapons is their size and the number of creatures required to operate them effectively (generally more than two). These weapons range from highly sophisticated cannons and rocket launchers to crude catapults and giant slingshots. Regardless of their form, they are all large enough that moving them is a slow process and labor-intensive enough to use that they require a team of creatures to operate them effectively.

## Repairing Weapons
If a weapon has taken damage but still has at least 1 hit point, a creature can spend 1 hour or more attempting to repair the damage. The creature must have the necessary tools and parts for the repairs. After 1 hour of repair work, the creature makes an Intelligence check, adding its proficiency bonus to the check if it is proficient with the required tools. If the check succeeds, the weapon regains 2d4 + the creature's Intelligence modifier + the creature's proficiency bonus hit points. If the check fails, the weapon does not regain any hit points, but the repair can be attempted again using the same tools and replacement parts.

\columnbreak

## Siege Weapon Attributes
In addition to the common attributes of size, weight, AC, HP, and damage immunity, these weapons have the following additional attributes and considerations:

### Hit Points 
A weapon has hit points that can be restored through repairs. When its hit points reach 0, the weapon becomes inoperative and irreparably damaged. 

Many weapons have a damage threshold. Any source of damage less than this threshold only inflicts superficial damage and doesn't lower the weapon's hit points.

### Weapon DC 
The weapon's DC is used whenever a creature makes a check to fix mishaps, when a creature is repairing the weapon, or the weapon forces a creature to make a saving throw.

### Challenge Rating
When players face enemies equipped with fully functioning siege weapons, the encounter's challenge rating (CR) should be calculated as if the weapon is an additional creature with its own CR.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/JjYPNWK/Unleash-Shell-The-Brothers-War-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-40px; right:0px; width:820px; transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:195px; right:100px; width:950px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(19deg)' />


<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:249px; right:-200px; width:900px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(0deg)' />



\pagebreakNum



### Ammo / Fuel
Weapons may require ammunition, such as bullets, or fuel, such as flammable chemicals, to make attacks. This part of the stat block includes the cost of the ammo and the number of charges it has, which represents the number of times the weapon can be used before it needs to be reloaded.

### Functions
By default, siege weapons have three different functions, which can each be activated as an action by its operators: Prep, Load, and Fire. Each function can only be performed once per round unless it states otherwise. Creatures within reach of a creature performing one of these functions can make opportunity attacks against them.

#### Prep
Siege weapons need to be prepped in different ways between being fired. This preparation could be cranking a ballista or cleaning the barrel of a cannon. Many siege weapons have multiple Prep functions that must be performed before they can be used again. In these cases, the different Prep actions can be done by different creatures within the same round. Unless stated otherwise, all the Prep functions must be completed before the weapon can be loaded.



##### Siege Weapons Art Credit
* Unleash Shell - Campbell White, Wizards of the Coast
* Goblin Artillery - Alex Horley-Orlandelli, Wizards of the Coast

\columnbreak

#### Load
This function is used to reload the weapon's ammunition up to its full capacity. It requires the creature loading it to have immediate access to the weapon's ammunition. If a creature doing the loading is hit by an opportunity it provoked by doing this, it drops the ammo and wastes its action.

#### Fire
This function is used to aim and fire the weapon at a target chosen by the creature performing the function.

### Passive Traits
This section describes any traits of the weapon has that don't require actions to utilize.

### Mishaps table
Some weapons can suffer a malfunction when certain functions are used. When such an event occurs, it will suffer a mishap and need to roll on its Mishap Table to determine what adverse effect it suffers. 

A creature can attempt to resolve a mishap by using its action to make an ability check based on the nature of the mishap. The creature making the check can be any member of the weapons team or anyone else within reach of the weapon. If the creature is proficient with the tools required for repairs and has them at hand, it adds its proficiency bonus to the check. A successful check ends the mishap. Mishaps that do not have a Repair Check Type cannot be repaired.

<img src='https://64.media.tumblr.com/97957bfd89fc58990ebbe31b4b543960/a95157cb330b1736-23/s1280x1920/c9807add3c7fc2bd781c456d1f8a9cee5de0f6e2.png' style='position:absolute; botom:-0px; right:0px; width:820px; transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-485px; right:-100px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(8deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />
